The Universal Scope of Divine Hearing and Sight
Dardir defines the third category of divine attributes: hearing and sight encompassing all existents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's attributes of hearing and sight encompass all existents, both pre-eternal and contingent, and are distinct from the attribute of knowledge.

Core Idea
Allah's hearing and sight cover everything that exists.

This lesson examines a crucial point in Islamic theology: the scope of divine hearing and sight. Many assume these attributes are limited to perceiving sounds and visible objects, but the classical doctrine asserts a far wider reach. Through this passage from Imam Dardir's commentary, we discover that hearing and sight attach to all existents—both eternal and contingent—revealing a comprehensive divine awareness that transcends ordinary sensory perception.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice how Dardir explicitly states that hearing and sight attach to 'every existent seen.'
Pay attention to the phrase 'تعلقا بكل موجود يُرى' (attach to every existent seen).
2
Understand the 'uncovering' (inkishāf)
Dardir explains that the attachment is one of 'uncovering' (inkishāf). Consider how this differs from the uncovering by knowledge.
Uncovering by hearing/sight is distinct from knowledge.
3
Grasp the universal scope
The passage clarifies that this includes both pre-eternal (God's essence and attributes) and contingent (creatures) existents.
This rejects limiting these attributes to only sounds and colors.
4
Internalize the distinctiveness
Dardir emphasizes that each attribute gives a different kind of uncovering, and both are different from knowledge.
This highlights the uniqueness of each divine attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقسم الثالث: ما يتعلق بجميع الموجودات (٢) ، وهو صفتان أيضًا، السمع والبصر، وإليه أشار بقوله: ٤٠ - واجزم بأنَّ سَمْعَهُ وَالبَصَرا * تعلَّقا بِكُلِّ مَوجُودِ يُرى (واجزِمْ) أَيُّها المُكَلِّفُ (بأنَّ سَمْعَهُ) تعالى والبصرا) الألفُ للإطلاقِ، (تعلقا) معا تعلق انكِشَافٍ بِكُلِّ مَوجودٍ يُرى) (۳) بالبناء للمجهول، أي: «يُعلَم»، أي: معلوم له السمع تعالى، قديماً كان كذاته وصفاته، أو حادثا كذَواتِ المخلوقينَ وصِفاتِهم. والانكشافُ بهما يغاير الانكشاف بالعِلم، وكذا الانكشافُ بكُلِّ منهما يغاير الانكشاف بالأخرى.
And the third category: that which attaches to all existents, and it is two attributes as well: hearing (as-samʿ) and sight (al-baṣar). And to this he [the author] alluded by his saying: 'And be certain that His hearing and sight attach to every existent seen (yurā).' (And be certain) O responsible person (that His hearing) exalted be He (and sight) – the alif is for release – (attach) together with an attachment of uncovering (inkishāf) (to every existent seen) – passive construction, i.e., 'is known' – i.e., it is known to His hearing, exalted be He, whether it is pre-eternal like His essence and attributes, or contingent like the essences of creatures and their attributes. And the uncovering by them is different from the uncovering by knowledge; likewise the uncovering by each of them is different from the uncovering by the other.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage defines the third category of divine attributes: those that attach to all existents. These are two attributes: hearing (samʿ) and sight (baṣar). The author quotes the verse: 'And be certain that His hearing and sight attach to every existent seen.' Then he explains: 'attach' means an attachment of uncovering (inkishāf) to every existent, whether pre-eternal (like God's essence and attributes) or contingent (like creatures and their attributes). This uncovering is distinct from the uncovering by knowledge (ʿilm), and each of hearing and sight gives a different kind of uncovering from the other. Thus, hearing and sight are not limited to sounds and visible objects but encompass all existing things.

Key Terms
السمع (as-samʿ)
البصر (al-baṣar)
تعلق (taʿalluq)
انكشاف (inkishāf)
الموجودات (al-mawjūdāt)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That hearing only relates to sounds and sight only to visible objects.
Correction: The passage states that hearing and sight attach to all existents, not limited to sounds or visible objects.

Checkpoint
According to Dardir, what do the attributes of hearing and sight attach to?
A) Only sounds and visible objects.
B) Only the actions of creatures.
C) All existents, both pre-eternal and contingent.
D) Only that which is known.

Key Takeaway
Allah's hearing and sight are not limited to sensory phenomena but encompass all existence, providing a comprehensive divine awareness distinct from knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The passage distinguishes between Allah's knowledge, hearing, and sight—each providing a different kind of uncovering. In your daily life, which of these three feels most real to you? How might you cultivate a deeper sense of being 'seen' by Allah, not just known?
?
Dardir says hearing and sight attach even to Allah's own essence and attributes. Does this notion of Allah 'hearing' His own attributes affect how you understand His closeness? What will you do this week to remind yourself that every moment is uncovered before His hearing and sight?

Divine Hearing and Sight Encompass All Existence
Dardeer classifies hearing and sight as attributes encompassing all existents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine hearing and sight encompass all existents in a unique way distinct from knowledge.

Core Idea
Divine hearing and sight disclose all existence uniquely.

This lesson explores the third category of divine attributes: hearing and sight, which, unlike some attributes that pertain only to certain things, encompass every existent. The commentary clarifies a key nuance: the term 'seen' in the poem actually means 'known,' extending the scope. We'll also see how disclosure through hearing and sight differs from knowledge and from each other.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the overall meaning. Notice how the poem and commentary work together.
Pay special attention to the parenthetical explanations in the translation.
2
Understand the clarification of 'yurā'
The commentary explains that 'yurā' (يُرى) in the poem is passive and means 'is known', not 'is seen'. This expands the scope of hearing and sight to all existents, not just visible objects.
This nuance is crucial for correct theological understanding.
3
Grasp the distinction between disclosure modes
The passage ends by stating that disclosure through hearing and sight differs from disclosure through knowledge, and also hearing differs from sight. Reflect on why these distinctions matter for divine attributes.
Each attribute has a unique mode of disclosing existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقسم الثالث: ما يتعلق بجميع الموجودات، وهو صفتان أيضًا، السمع والبصر، وإليه أشار بقوله: ٤٠ - واجزم بأنَّ سَمْعَهُ وَالبَصَرا * تعلَّقا بِكُلِّ مَوجُودِ يُرى (واجزِمْ) أَيُّها المُكَلِّفُ (بأنَّ سَمْعَهُ) تعالى والبصرا) الألفُ للإطلاقِ، (تعلقا) معا تعلق انكِشَافٍ بِكُلِّ مَوجودٍ يُرى) بالبناء للمجهول، أي: «يُعلَم»، أي: معلوم له السمع تعالى، قديماً كان كذاته وصفاته، أو حادثا كذَواتِ المخلوقينَ وصِفاتِهم. والانكشافُ بهما يغاير الانكشاف بالعِلم، وكذا الانكشافُ بكُلِّ منهما يغاير تعلقات الانكشاف بالأخرى.
And the third category: what pertains to all existent things, and it is two attributes as well: hearing and sight. And to it he alluded by his saying: 'And be certain that His hearing and sight are related to every existent thing that is seen.' (And be certain) O responsible person (that His hearing) Exalted is He (and sight) – the alif is for release – (are related) together with a relation of disclosure to every existent thing that is seen, in the passive voice, i.e., 'is known', meaning: known to Him – hearing and sight of the Exalted – whether eternal like His essence and attributes, or temporal like the essences of creatures and their attributes. And disclosure by them differs from disclosure by knowledge, and likewise disclosure by each of them differs from the relations of disclosure by the other.

Commentary
This passage classifies the third category of divine attributes: hearing and sight, which pertain to all existent things. The poet states that these attributes are related to every existent thing that is 'seen' (yurā). However, the commentator explains that 'seen' here is passive, meaning 'known' (yu'lam), so it includes all existents—whether eternal, like Allah's own essence and attributes, or temporal, like the essences and attributes of creatures. The passage then highlights that the disclosure (inkishāf) through hearing and sight is different from disclosure through knowledge, and also the disclosure through hearing differs from that through sight. This underscores the distinctness of each attribute.

Divine Hearing and Sight: Difference in Attachment
Dardeer contrasts divine and human hearing/sight in attachment scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how divine hearing and sight differ from human hearing and sight in terms of their objects of attachment (ta‘alluq).

Core Idea
Divine hearing and sight encompass all existents; human senses are limited to specific physical conditions.

Imam Dardeer explains that while divine hearing and sight are all-encompassing, human hearing and sight are restricted to certain types of beings and conditions. This lesson focuses on the first contrast: the scope and conditions of attachment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on attachment
Read the Arabic passage once to get the overall meaning, then read the translation. Notice the contrast between 'hears and sees essences and attributes' and the limitations of human senses.
Focus on the words 'في التعلق' and the conditions mentioned.
2
Identify the specific limitations
List the conditions under which human hearing and sight operate according to the passage: hearing only sounds and not too far; sight only bodies/colors, specific direction and manner.
3
Contrast with divine hearing and sight
Consider how divine hearing and sight have no such restrictions—they attach to all existents, whether sounds or not, and without physical conditions. This shows their perfection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الأول: الإلهيات ومتعلقهما أخصُّ مِنْ مُتعلقِ العِلم ، فيسمع ويرى سُبحانَهُ الذُّواتِ والصَّفاتِ، كانتْ مِن قبيل الأصوات أو مِنْ غَيرها ، فسمعه وبصره تعالى يخالفان سمْعَنا وبصرنا في التعلقِ؛ لأنَّ سَمْعَنا إنما يتعلق عادة بعض الموجودات، وهي الأصواتُ، بَشَرْطِ عدم البُعْدِ جدا، وبصَرُنا إنما يتعلقُ عادةً ببعض الموجودات، وهي الأجسام وألوانها، في جهةٍ مخصوصة على وجه مخصوص. كما أنهما يُخالفان سمعنا وبصَرَنا أيضًا في الذات، فهما صفتان قديمتان قائمتان بذاته تعالى، وأما سمعنا وبصَرُنا فحادثانِ قائمانِ بِمَحَلَ مخصوص: فبصَرُنا قائم بإنسان العين، أو هو قوة مودعة في العصبتَينِ المجوفتين اللتين يتلاقيان ثُمَّ يفترقان، كما هو مذهب الحكماء، وسمْعُنا قائم بالصَّحَاحَ، أَيْ: ثُقْبُ الْأُذُنِ، أَو هو قوةٌ قائِمَةٌ بالعصب المفروش في مُقَعَّرِ الصَّماخ. والله تعالى منزّه عن ذلك، وسَمْعُنا وبَصَرُنا مِنْ أسباب عُلومِنا، بخلافِ سمْعِه وبصره تعالى.
The first section: The Divine Matters. And their objects of attachment are more specific than the object of knowledge, so He – exalted is He – hears and sees essences and attributes, whether they are of the type of sounds or otherwise. So His hearing and sight differ from our hearing and sight in attachment, because our hearing ordinarily attaches only to some existents, namely sounds, with the condition of not being too far, and our sight ordinarily attaches only to some existents, namely bodies and their colors, in a specific direction in a specific manner. Also, they differ from our hearing and sight in essence, for they are two eternal attributes subsisting in His essence, whereas our hearing and sight are temporal subsisting in a specific locus: our sight subsists in the pupil of the eye, or it is a power deposited in the two hollow nerves which meet then separate, as is the view of the philosophers; and our hearing subsists in the ear-hole, i.e., the opening of the ear, or it is a power subsisting in the nerve spread in the hollow of the auditory canal. Allah is exalted above that. And our hearing and sight are among the causes of our knowledge, unlike His hearing and sight.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage contrasts divine hearing and sight with human ones in two respects: attachment (ta‘alluq) and essence (dhāt). First, in attachment: divine hearing and sight are more specific than knowledge but still encompass all existents (essences and attributes, whether sounds or not). Human hearing is limited to sounds with proximity; human sight is limited to bodies and colors with direction and condition. Second, in essence: divine hearing and sight are eternal attributes subsisting in Allah’s essence, while human hearing and sight are temporal and subsist in specific bodily loci—sight in the pupil or optic nerves, hearing in the ear canal or auditory nerve, according to philosophers. Allah is transcendent above such bodily locations. Additionally, human hearing and sight are causes of our knowledge, whereas divine hearing and sight are not causes of His knowledge (since His knowledge is eternal and uncaused).

Key Terms
تعلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Sounds must be loud
B) Sounds must not be too far
C) Sounds must be in a specific direction
D) Sounds must be essences

Key Takeaway
Divine hearing and sight encompass all existents without restriction, whereas human senses are limited to specific physical objects and conditions.

Divine Hearing and Sight: Difference in Essence
Dardeer contrasts divine and human hearing/sight in essence (eternal vs temporal) and locus.

Core Idea

Three Relations of Divine Hearing and Sight
Dardeer enumerates the three types of relations of divine hearing and sight

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three types of relations of divine hearing and sight, and why they are necessary to account for both the divine self and creation.

Core Idea
Divine hearing and sight relate to everything, whether actual, potential, divine, or created.

Dardeer now shows that Allah's hearing and sight are not limited to one kind of relation. They relate to His own essence, to potential creatures, and to actual creatures. This tripartite division ensures that these attributes are comprehensive and complete.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic once without analyzing. Then read the translation to get the overall meaning.
2
Identify each of the three relations
List the three relations in order, noting their labels: tanzīzī qadīm, ṣulūḥī qadīm, and tanzīzī ḥādith.
Notice that the first two are eternal, the third is temporal.
3
Understand what each relation covers
The first relates to Allah Himself, the second to potential creatures, the third to actual creatures. Ask why each is needed.
This shows divine knowledge encompasses everything.
4
Connect to the misconception
Reflect on the common misunderstanding that divine hearing/sight only relate to actual existents. This passage corrects that by including a potential relation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهما تعلقات ثلاثة : ١- تنجيزي قديم بذاته وصفاته تعالى، ۲- وصلوحي قديم بذواتنا وصفاتنا، ۳- وتنجيزي حادث عِندَ وُجودِنا.
And for them (hearing and sight) there are three relations: 1- An eternal actual relation to His essence and attributes; 2- An eternal potential relation to our essences and attributes; 3- A temporal actual relation at the time of our existence.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage enumerates three types of relations (ta‘alluqāt) for divine hearing and sight. First, an eternal actual relation (tanzīzī qadīm) to Allah's own essence and attributes—He hears and sees Himself and His attributes from eternity. Second, an eternal potential relation (ṣulūḥī qadīm) to the essences and attributes of creatures before they exist—they are potentially hearable and seeable by Allah. Third, a temporal actual relation (tanzīzī ḥādith) at the moment of our existence—when creatures come into being, He actually hears and sees them. This tripartite division shows the comprehensiveness of these attributes: they cover the divine self, the potential for creation, and actual creation.

Key Terms
تعلقات
تنجيزي
صلوحي
قديم
حادث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Divine hearing and sight only relate to things that actually exist.
Correction: The second type (eternal potential relation) shows they also relate to non-existent creatures potentially.

C) Eternal potential relation to our essences
D) Temporal potential relation to our attributes

Key Takeaway
Divine hearing and sight have three relations: eternal actual to Allah's self, eternal potential to creatures before existence, and temporal actual to creatures after creation.

The Difference Between Divine and Human Hearing and Sight
Dardeer contrasts divine and human hearing/sight in relation and essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the divine attributes of hearing and sight differ from human senses in both their essence and their mode of relation.

Core Idea
God's hearing and sight are eternal and unlimited; human senses are temporal and conditioned.

Imam Dardeer begins by specifying that the divine attributes of hearing and sight relate to a more specific domain than the attribute of knowledge. He then emphasizes that God's hearing and sight are fundamentally different from ours—not just in degree but in essence. This lesson explores those key differences, showing that divine perception is not bound by the physical limitations that constrain human senses.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let Dardeer's contrast between divine and human perception come through.
Notice the phrase 'يخالفان سمعنا وبصرنا' — they differ from our hearing and sight.
2
Identify the two dimensions of difference
The text distinguishes difference in relation (fi al-taʿalluq) and difference in essence (fi al-dhāt). Find where each is discussed.
Relation: human senses are limited to certain objects under conditions. Essence: human senses are temporal and subsist in organs.
3
Note the implication for knowledge
Dardeer states that human senses are causes of knowledge, but divine senses are not. Think about why this matters for understanding God's attributes.
This reinforces that God's knowledge is not derived from His senses, unlike ours.
4
Reflect on the overall point
Summarize in your own words the core contrast Dardeer is making between divine and human hearing/sight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الأول: الإلهيات. ومتعلقهما أخصُّ مِنْ مُتعلقِ العِلم ، فيسمع ويرى سُبحانَهُ الذُّواتِ والصَّفاتِ، كانتْ مِن قبيل الأصوات أو مِنْ غَيرها ، فسمعه وبصره تعالى يخالفان سمْعَنا وبصرنا في التعلقِ؛ لأنَّ سَمْعَنا إنما يتعلق عادة ببعض الموجودات، وهي الأصواتُ، بَشَرْطِ عدم البُعْدِ جدا، وبصَرُنا إنما يتعلقُ عادةً ببعض الموجودات، وهي الأجسام وألوانها، في جهةٍ مخصوصة على وجه مخصوص. كما أنهما يُخالفان سمعنا وبصَرَنا أيضًا في الذات، فهما صفتان قديمتان قائمتان بذاته تعالى، وأما سمعنا وبصَرُنا فحادثانِ قائمانِ بِمَحَلَ مخصوص: فبصَرُنا قائم بإنسان العين، أو هو قوة مودعة في العصبتَينِ المجوفتين اللتين يتلاقيان ثُمَّ يفترقان، كما هو مذهب الحكماء، وسمْعُنا قائم بالصَّحَاحَ، أَيْ: ثُقْبُ الْأُذُنِ، أَو هو قوةٌ قائِمَةٌ بالعصب المفروش في مُقَعَّرِ الصَّماخ. والله تعالى منزّه عن ذلك، وسَمْعُنا وبَصَرُنا مِنْ أسباب عُلومِنا، بخلافِ سمْعِه وبصره تعالى. ولهما تعلقات ثلاثة : ١- تنجيزي قديم بذاته وصفاته تعالى، ۲- وصلوحي قديم بذواتنا وصفاتنا، ۳- وتنجيزي حادث عِندَ وُجودِنا.
The first section: Divine Matters. And their (hearing and sight) relation is more specific than the relation of knowledge, so He hears and sees, glory be to Him, essences and attributes, whether they are of the category of sounds or otherwise. So His hearing and sight, exalted is He, differ from our hearing and sight in relation; because our hearing only relates ordinarily to some existents, which are sounds, with the condition of not being too distant, and our sight only relates ordinarily to some existents, which are bodies and their colors, in a specific direction on a specific manner. And also they differ from our hearing and sight in essence, for they are two eternal attributes subsisting by His essence, exalted is He. As for our hearing and sight, they are temporal, subsisting in a specific locus: our sight subsists in the pupil of the eye, or it is a power deposited in the two hollow nerves that meet then separate, as is the doctrine of the philosophers. And our hearing subsists in the tympanum, i.e., the ear hole, or it is a power subsisting by the nerve spread in the cavity of the ear canal. And God, exalted is He, is free from that. And our hearing and sight are causes of our knowledge, unlike His hearing and sight, exalted is He. And they have three relations: 1) a commencing eternal (relation) to His essence and attributes, 2) a potential eternal (relation) to our essences and attributes, and 3) a commencing temporal (relation) at the time of our existence.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a definition and comparison of the divine attributes of hearing (samʿ) and sight (baṣar) with human hearing and sight. The author begins by stating that these two divine attributes relate to a more specific range than the attribute of knowledge: knowledge encompasses everything, while hearing and sight pertain only to existent things (al-dhāt wa al-ṣifāt). God hears sounds and sees objects, whether they are sounds or not. Then he explains the difference in modality: human hearing ordinarily requires sounds to be not too distant; human sight requires bodies at a certain distance, with line of sight, etc. In contrast, divine hearing and sight are not limited by such conditions. He then contrasts the essence: God's hearing and sight are eternal (qadīmān) and subsist by His essence, while human hearing and sight are temporal (ḥādithān) and subsist in specific bodily organs—the ear and eye. He mentions two philosophical views on the nature of these organs (the power in the nerves or the physical structure). He emphasizes that God is free from such physical limitations. Furthermore, human senses are causes of our knowledge (we learn through them), but God's hearing and sight are not causes of His knowledge because His knowledge is eternal and uncaused. Finally, he enumerates three types of relation (taʿalluq) that the divine hearing and sight have: (1) an eternal commencing relation to God's own essence and attributes, (2) an eternal potential relation to created essences and attributes (i.e., before they exist, God's hearing and sight can potentially relate to them), and (3) a temporal commencing relation at the moment of our existence (when we and our actions come into being, God's hearing and sight actually relate to them). This classification shows that divine perception is not dependent on our presence but is eternal in its capacity.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's hearing and sight are like human senses but without physical organs.
Correction: Dardeer clarifies that the difference is not just in organs but also in essence: human senses are temporal and limited in relation, while God's are eternal and unlimited. They differ in both their nature and their operation.

Checkpoint
According to Dardeer, in what two ways do divine hearing and sight differ from human hearing and sight?
A) In relation and in essence
B) In time and in location
C) In organ and in power
D) In knowledge and in will

Key Takeaway
God's hearing and sight are fundamentally different from human senses: they are eternal, unlimited, and not derived from physical organs or external conditions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you speak or act in secret, do you truly believe that God hears and sees you in a way that is unconstrained by distance or conditions? How would your private behavior change if you lived with that reality every moment? Challenge: start today by pausing before any private action and consciously affirming that God is hearing and seeing.
?
Your hearing and sight are temporal and finite — they will cease at death. Yet you spend most of your energy pursuing things perceived by these senses. Is your attachment to the seen world actually a form of forgetfulness that God's sight alone is eternal? Ask yourself: What one thing today can you value not because you see it, but because God sees it?
?
The passage says our hearing and sight are causes of our knowledge, but God's are not. Do you rely on your senses as the ultimate source of truth, or do you submit to what God has revealed even when it contradicts your sensory experience? Take a concrete example from your life where your senses told you one thing and revelation told you another — which did you follow?

Divine Attributes

The Three Relations of Divine Hearing and Sight
Dardeer lists three relations of divine hearing and sight with explanations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three types of relation that the divine attributes of hearing and sight have to God's essence and to creation.

Core Idea
Divine hearing and sight relate to everything in three ways: eternal to God, potential to creation, and actual at the moment of existence.

After establishing that God's hearing and sight are unlike human senses, Imam Dardeer presents a precise classification of how these attributes relate to different objects. He enumerates three distinct relations that cover both the eternal and temporal domains. This lesson unpacks that classification and its theological significance.

Guided Path
1
Examine the three relations
Read the passage listing the three relations. Notice that each has a name (tunjīzī or ṣulūḥī) and a temporal qualifier (qadīm or ḥādith).
2
Understand the first relation
The first relation is 'tunjīzī qadīm' (commencing eternal) and pertains to God's own essence and attributes. This means God always hears and sees Himself and His attributes essentially.
This is an internal relation, independent of creation.
3
Understand the second relation
The second is 'ṣulūḥī qadīm' (potential eternal) and relates to our essences and attributes. Before we exist, God's hearing and sight have the capacity to relate to us, but not yet in actuality.
'Potential' here means readiness, not passivity.
4
Understand the third relation
The third is 'tunjīzī ḥādith' (commencing temporal) which occurs at the moment of our existence. When we come into being, God actually hears and sees us and our actions.
This actual relation is temporal because it begins with our existence.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this classification matters. It shows that God's hearing and sight are not dependent on creation for their actuality, but they are still genuinely related to created things in a way that respects God's eternity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الأول: الإلهيات. ومتعلقهما أخصُّ مِنْ مُتعلقِ العِلم ، فيسمع ويرى سُبحانَهُ الذُّواتِ والصَّفاتِ، كانتْ مِن قبيل الأصوات أو مِنْ غَيرها ، فسمعه وبصره تعالى يخالفان سمْعَنا وبصرنا في التعلقِ؛ لأنَّ سَمْعَنا إنما يتعلق عادة ببعض الموجودات، وهي الأصواتُ، بَشَرْطِ عدم البُعْدِ جدا، وبصَرُنا إنما يتعلقُ عادةً ببعض الموجودات، وهي الأجسام وألوانها، في جهةٍ مخصوصة على وجه مخصوص. كما أنهما يُخالفان سمعنا وبصَرَنا أيضًا في الذات، فهما صفتان قديمتان قائمتان بذاته تعالى، وأما سمعنا وبصَرُنا فحادثانِ قائمانِ بِمَحَلَ مخصوص: فبصَرُنا قائم بإنسان العين، أو هو قوة مودعة في العصبتَينِ المجوفتين اللتين يتلاقيان ثُمَّ يفترقان، كما هو مذهب الحكماء، وسمْعُنا قائم بالصَّحَاحَ، أَيْ: ثُقْبُ الْأُذُنِ، أَو هو قوةٌ قائِمَةٌ بالعصب المفروش في مُقَعَّرِ الصَّماخ. والله تعالى منزّه عن ذلك، وسَمْعُنا وبَصَرُنا مِنْ أسباب عُلومِنا، بخلافِ سمْعِه وبصره تعالى. ولهما تعلقات ثلاثة : ١- تنجيزي قديم بذاته وصفاته تعالى، ۲- وصلوحي قديم بذواتنا وصفاتنا، ۳- وتنجيزي حادث عِندَ وُجودِنا.

?

Divine Attributes

The Eternity of Attributes and Refutation of Mu'tazila
Imam Dardeer explains the meaning of 'eternal by the essence' for attributes and refutes Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni doctrine that divine attributes are eternal by themselves—neither caused by the essence nor identical to it—and how this refutes the Mu'tazila position.

Core Idea
Divine attributes are eternal by themselves, not caused by or separate from the Essence.

Imam Dardeer lays out the Sunni position on the eternity of attributes, clarifying a subtle but crucial point: attributes like power and knowledge are eternal not because the essence causes them, but because they are inherent to the essence and inseparable from it. He then refutes two errors: the view that attributes are caused by the essence (which some Ash'aris held) and the Mu'tazila denial of distinct attributes. This passage establishes the middle path between identification and separation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Get an overview of the complete argument. Note the key phrase: 'and all of them are eternal by the essence because they are not other than the essence.'
Pay attention to the poetic line quoted at the start.
2
Understand 'eternal by the essence'
Focus on the first explanation: it means the attributes are eternal by themselves, not that their eternity is derived from the essence being a cause. The author rejects both the view that attributes are possible in themselves and that the essence is a cause.
The author calls the causal view 'a hideous statement'.
3
Grasp the inseparable but non-identical relation
Attributes are not 'other than' the essence in the sense of being separable; the essence cannot be conceived without them, nor can they exist apart. Yet they are not identical to the essence, otherwise life would be knowledge.
4
Examine the Mu'tazila objection and answer
The Mu'tazila deny additional attributes to avoid multiplicity of eternal entities. The answer: multiplicity of attributes in one essence is not impossible; only multiplicity of essences is.
This is the standard Sunni refutation.
5
Reflect on the middle path
The Sunni position avoids both extremes: attributes are neither created nor caused (like Mu'tazila) nor identical to the essence (like Jahmiyya). They are eternal by themselves, inseparable yet distinct.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١ ٤ - وكُلُّها قديمةٌ بالذاتِ * لأنها ليستْ بغَير الذات ( وكلُّها) أي: صفات المعاني (قديمة بالذاتِ) أي: بذاتها، أي: إِنَّ قِدَمَها ذات صفات وليستْ بِمُمْكِنةٍ في نفْسِها، وإِنَّما قِدَمُها بِقِدَمِ الذاتِ المُقَدَّسِ، أو أنَّ ذاته تعالى علة فيها، كما قال بذلك بعضُ عُلَماء أهْلِ السُّنَةِ)، وهو قول شنيع، تُجه قُلُوبُ الصالحين قديمة العارفين بربهم، إذ لا يخفى ما فيه مِنْ إساءة الأدب بمقامِ اللهِ الأَعَزّ الأحمى، مَعَ أَنَّه لا حُجَّةَ على ارتكابه، بل الحجّةُ قائمة على ما ذكرنا، كما أشرتُ له بقولي: المعاني كلها (لأنها ليستْ بغَيرِ الذاتِ العَليّةِ، بمعنى أنها لا تنفك عنها، فلا يُعقَلُ قيامُ الذاتِ بدونها، ولا وُجودها في غَيرِ الذات المقدَّسِ، فلا يصِحُ القَولُ بأنها ممكنةٌ في نفْسِها، أو أنَّ الذات العليَّةَ عِلَّةٌ فيها. وكما أنها ليستْ بغَير الذاتِ لَيستْ بعينها أيضًا، وهو واضح، وإلا لزِمَ أنْ تكونَ الذاتُ صفات، وأنَّ الحَياةَ عَينُ العِلْمِ مَثَلًا، وهو باطل، فبطَلَ ما ذهَبَ إلَيه المُعْتَزِلَةُ، مِنْ أنه تعالى قادر بذاتِه، وحي بذاتِه، وعالم كذلك، وهكذا، لا بصفات زائدة على الذاتِ تُسَمّى بالقُدْرة والحياة، وهكذا، لئلا يلزَمَ تعَدُّدُ القُدّماءِ المحال. والجواب: أنَّ المُحالَ إنما هو تعدُّدُ ذَواتِ، أَمَا ذاتٌ واحدةٌ متَّصِفةٌ بصفاتٍ لا يصِحُ الانفكاك عنها فليس بمُحال، بل هو الواجب. وإنما اقتصرنا على الأول؛ لأننا في مقام الاستدلال على أنَّ قِدَمَها ذات.
14. And all of them are eternal by the essence * because they are not other than the essence. (And all of them) i.e., attributes of meanings (eternal by the essence) i.e., by themselves, i.e., that their eternity is a characteristic of attributes and they are not possible in themselves, but rather their eternity is through the eternity of the sacred essence, or that His essence, exalted is He, is a cause in them, as said by some scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah), and it is a hideous statement; the hearts of the righteous are repelled by it, [??] of the knowers of their Lord, for it is not hidden what is in it of disrespect to the station of God, the Most Mighty, the Most Protected, although there is no proof for undertaking it, but rather the proof is established on what we have mentioned, as I indicated with my saying: all the attributes (because they are not other than the lofty essence, meaning they are inseparable from it, so the subsistence of the essence without them cannot be conceived, nor their existence in other than the sacred essence. So the saying that they are possible in themselves, or that the lofty essence is a cause in them, is invalid. And just as they are not other than the essence, they are also not identical to it, and that is clear. Otherwise it would necessitate that the essence be attributes, and that life is identical to knowledge, for example, and that is false. So what the Mu'tazila went to is nullified: that He, exalted is He, is powerful by His essence, living by His essence, knowing likewise, etc., without attributes additional to the essence called power and life, etc., to avoid the impossible multiplicity of eternal entities. And the answer: the impossible is only multiplicity of essences; as for one essence qualified by attributes that cannot be separated from it, that is not impossible, but rather it is necessary. And we only limited ourselves to the first because we are in the position of proving that their eternity is [self].
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument defending the Sunni position on the divine attributes (ṣifāt al-maʿānī). The author begins by quoting the verse of the poem: 'And all of them are eternal by the essence because they are not other than the essence.' He then explains that 'all of them' refers to the attributes of meanings (such as power, knowledge, life). 'Eternal by the essence' means they are eternal by themselves (bi-dhātihā), not that their eternity is derived from the essence being a cause. He refutes two erroneous views: (1) that their eternity is only by the eternity of the essence (i.e., they are possible in themselves and only became eternal because the essence is eternal), and (2) that the essence is a cause for them. He condemns these as a hideous statement (qawl shanīʿ) that repels the hearts of the righteous, as it implies disrespect. He then reinforces the correct view: the attributes are not other than the essence in the sense that they are inseparable; the essence cannot be conceived without them, nor can they exist apart from the essence. Therefore, they are not possible in themselves, nor is the essence a cause for them. Additionally, they are not identical to the essence, for if they were, then the essence would be attributes and, for example, life would be identical to knowledge, which is false. This refutes the Mu'tazila who deny additional attributes, claiming that God is powerful by His essence (without a separate attribute of power) to avoid multiplicity of eternal entities. The author responds: the impossible multiplicity is that of essences (i.e., multiple gods), but one essence qualified by inseparable attributes is not only possible but necessary for the Necessary Being. The passage concludes by stating that they limit the discussion to the first part (that they are not other than the essence) because the context is proving that the attributes are eternal by themselves (qidamuhā dhātī). The commentary thus establishes the Sunni creed that attributes are eternal and neither identical to nor separate from the essence, and avoids both the extremes of the Mu'tazila (denial of distinct attributes) and the view that attributes are created or caused by the essence.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'eternal by the essence' means the essence is a cause for the attributes, making them dependent on the essence.
Correction: The author clarifies that 'eternal by the essence' means the attributes are eternal by themselves, not caused by the essence. The attributes are inseparable from the essence but not caused by it.

Checkpoint

A) Because it affirms too many attributes
B) Because it denies additional attributes to avoid multiplicity of eternal entities, but multiplicity of attributes in one essence is not impossible
C) Because it claims attributes are created
D) Because it equates life with knowledge

Key Takeaway
The eternity of attributes is intrinsic to the divine essence, and affirming multiple distinct attributes does not imply multiplicity of gods.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?

The Attributes Are Eternal by the Essence
Dardeer defines the eternity of attributes and refutes opposing views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the divine attributes are described as 'eternal by the essence' and why they cannot be considered possible in themselves or caused by the essence.

Core Idea
The attributes are inseparable from Allah's essence—neither possible nor caused.

In this passage, Imam Dardeer explains a key doctrine of Sunni theology: the divine attributes are eternal by the essence, not by any external cause. He clarifies what this means and refutes two misunderstandings—that the attributes are possible in themselves or that the essence is a cause for them. This sets the foundation for understanding Allah's attributes as necessary, not contingent.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the translation. Notice the poetic line and commentary.
The commentary expands on the line 'And all of them are eternal by the essence'.
2
Understand 'eternal by the essence'
Dardeer explains that the attributes' eternity is intrinsic to them; they are not possible in themselves, nor is the essence a cause. Identify his strong condemnation of the causal view.
He calls the causal view 'vile' and 'ill-mannered'.
3
Grasp the proof: 'because they are not other than the essence'
The attributes are inseparable from the essence. This refutes both possibility and causality. They are not other, nor identical.
If they were other, they could be separate; if identical, then attributes would collapse into essence.
4
See the refutation of Mu'tazila
The Mu'tazila deny additional attributes to avoid multiplicity of eternals. Dardeer answers: multiplicity of essences is impossible, but multiple attributes within one essence is necessary.
This is a key theological debate.

المعاني
كلها
(لأنها ليستْ بغَيرِ الذاتِ العَليّةِ، بمعنى أنها لا تنفك عنها، فلا يُعقَلُ قيامُ الذاتِ بدونها، ولا وُجودها في غَيرِ الذات المقدَّسِ، فلا يصِحُ القَولُ بأنها ممكنةٌ في نفْسِها، أو أنَّ الذات العليَّةَ عِلَّةٌ فيها. وكما أنها ليستْ بغَير الذاتِ لَيستْ بعينها أيضًا، وهو واضح، وإلا لزِمَ أنْ تكونَ الذاتُ صفات، وأنَّ الحَياةَ عَينُ العِلْمِ مَثَلًا، وهو باطل، فبطَلَ ما ذهَبَ إلَيه المُعْتَزِلَةُ، مِنْ أنه تعالى قادر بذاتِه، وحي بذاتِه، وعالم كذلك، وهكذا، لا بصفات زائدة على الذاتِ تُسَمّى بالقُدْرة والحياة، وهكذا، لئلا يلزَمَ تَعَدُّدُ القُدّماءِ المحال. والجواب: أنَّ المُحالَ إنما هو تعَدُّدُ ذَواتِ، أَمَا ذاتٌ واحدةٌ متَّصِفةٌ بصفاتٍ لا يصِحُ الانفكاك عنها فليس بمُحال، بل هو الواجب. وإنما اقتصرنا على الأول؛ لأننا في مقام الاستدلال على أنَّ قِدَمَها ذات.
Explanation of Al-Kharidat Al-Bahiyyah. 14 And all of them are eternal by the essence * because they are not other than the essence. (And all of them) i.e., the attributes of meanings (eternal by the essence) i.e., by their essence, meaning that their eternity is the essence of the attributes, and they are not possible in themselves, rather their eternity is by the eternity of the sacred essence, or that His exalted essence is a cause in them, as some scholars of Ahl al-Sunna said that, and it is a vile statement, it pains the hearts of the righteous and the feet of the knowers of their Lord, for what it contains of ill-manners towards the station of the most mighty and most protected God is not hidden, and there is no evidence for adopting it, rather the evidence stands for what we mentioned, as I indicated with my saying: the attributes, all of them (because they are not other than the exalted essence, meaning that they are not separate from it, so the existence of the essence without them is not conceivable, nor their existence in other than the sacred essence, so it is not valid to say that they are possible in themselves, or that the exalted essence is a cause in them. And just as they are not other than the essence, they are also not identical to it, and that is clear, otherwise it would necessitate that the essence be attributes, and that life be identical to knowledge, for example, and that is false. So what the Mu'tazila went to is false, that He is powerful by His essence, living by His essence, knowing likewise, and so on, not by attributes additional to the essence called power, life, etc., lest the impossible multiplicity of the eternals occur. The answer: the impossible is only multiplicity of essences, but one essence qualified by attributes from which separation is not valid is not impossible, rather it is necessary. And we restricted to the first because we are in the context of demonstrating that their eternity is [by] the essence.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage defines the eternity of the attributes and refutes objections. The author begins by explaining the line 'And all of them are eternal by the essence', meaning the attributes of meanings (صفات المعاني) are eternal by their essence, i.e., their eternity is not due to being possible in themselves, nor is the divine essence a cause for them. He strongly condemns the view that the essence is a cause, saying it is a vile statement that pains the hearts and feet of the righteous and knowers. Then he explains the reason given in the poem: 'because they are not other than the essence', meaning the attributes are inseparable from the essence. He refutes two false conclusions: that the attributes are possible in themselves, and that the essence is a cause. He also refutes the Mu'tazila who deny additional attributes by arguing that multiplicity of eternals (تعدد القدماء) is impossible; but the answer is that multiplicity of essences is impossible, not multiplicity of attributes within one essence. The passage ends by noting that they only focused on the first point because they are proving the eternity of the attributes by the essence.

Key Terms
صفات المعاني
قديمة بالذات
ممكنة
علة
المعتزلة
تعدد القدماء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'eternal by the essence' means the attributes are independent essences or that the divine essence is a cause for them.
Correction: The attributes are not independent; they are inseparable from the essence and not caused by it. Their eternity is intrinsic, not derived from an external cause.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Dardeer, what is the correct understanding of 'the attributes are eternal by the essence'?
A) The attributes are possible in themselves but made eternal by God.
B) The divine essence is a cause for the attributes' existence.
C) The attributes are inseparable from the essence and not possible in themselves.
D) The attributes are identical to the essence.

Key Takeaway
The divine attributes are eternal by the essence, meaning they are intrinsic and inseparable from Allah—neither possible nor caused, and not identical to the essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that your limited understanding of Allah's attributes might lead you to think of them as separate 'parts' of Allah? How does Dardeer's insistence that they are 'not other than the essence but not identical' confront your own mental images of Allah? What will you do to purify your conception of Him starting today?
?
Dardeer calls the view that the essence is a cause for the attributes 'vile' and 'ill-mannered'. Examine your own heart: have you ever thought of Allah's attributes as something He 'has' like you have a car, or as tools He uses? What does that reveal about your adab (etiquette) towards Allah? Commit to one specific way you will correct this mindset today.
?
The Mu'tazila feared multiplicity of eternals and thus denied the attributes. Is there any truth you have been afraid to accept because it seemed to conflict with Allah's oneness or unity? Dardeer shows that unity does not mean simplicity or emptiness. What attribute of Allah do you need to affirm more boldly in your life, even if it challenges your assumptions? How will you act on that this week?

Divine Speech is Internal, Not Composed of Letters and Sounds
Dardeer explains that God's speech is internal (نفسي), not composed of letters and sounds, refuting opposing views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ahl al-Sunna affirm that Allah's speech is an eternal internal attribute, distinct from created verbal speech, and how this resolves objections against divine speech.

Core Idea
Allah's speech is not like ours; it is an eternal inner attribute without letters or sounds.

This passage tackles a central theological question: Does Allah speak in the same way humans do? The Mu'tazila argued that speech requires letters and sounds, which are created, so Allah cannot truly speak. Ahl al-Sunna respond by distinguishing between verbal speech (لفظي) and internal speech (نفسي), affirming that Allah's attribute of speech is internal and eternal, free from temporal composition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get an overview of the argument. Notice how Dardeer contrasts the Mu'tazila position with that of Ahl al-Sunna.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila objection
Find where the Mu'tazila claim is presented: that speech requires letters, sounds, and arrangement, all of which are created. They conclude that Allah cannot be described as speaking, and reinterpret scriptural verses accordingly.
Their reinterpretation is that Allah creates speech in something else, like the tree for Moses.
3
Understand the Ahl al-Sunna solution
Ahl al-Sunna deny that speech is confined to letters and sounds. They divide speech into two types: verbal (لفظي) and internal (نفسي). Allah's attribute is internal speech, which is not composed of letters or sounds and is eternal.
This avoids attributing created things (like letters) to Allah.
4
Note the additional refutations
Dardeer also refutes the Karramiyya and Hanabila who claim Allah's speech is a created accident of sounds/letters, even if eternal. The internal speech is not such an accident.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ الكلامُ لَيسَ بالحروفِ * ولَيسَ بالترتيب كالمألوف وما ذهب المعتزلة إلى استحالة الكلامِ عليه تعالى، لأنه إنما يكونُ بحُروفِ وأصوات، وتقديم وتأخير، وغير ذلك، وهذه كلها حادثة، ولا يصح اتصافه تعالى بالحوادث، وإلا لكان حادثا، وصرَفوا ما ورَدَ في الكتاب والسُّنْةِ، مِنْ أنه تعالى متكلم عن ظاهره، على معنى أنه خالق الكلام في غيره، كالشَّجَرَةِ التي كلّمت موسى العليا مثلا، فالكلامُ صِفةٌ غَيره لا صفَتُه تعالى.. أَجَابَ أَهْلُ السُّنَّةِ بِمَنْعِ حَضْرِ الكَلام في الحروفِ والأصوات، بجعل الكلامِ قسمين: لفظي ونفسي، والثاني هو المراد، كما أشار إليه بقوله:
(ثُمَّ الكلام) أي: كلامه تعالى، الذي هو صفةُ ذاتِه، نفْسِي، (لَيسَ بالحروف) والأصوات)، (ولَيسَ) مُتلَبّسا (بالترتيب) مِنْ تقديم وتأخير، (ك) الكلام الحادث (المألوف) لنا، وحينَئِذٍ فلا يلزم المحالُ. وفي قولي: «وليسَ بالحروفِ... إلخ» ردُّ أيضًا على الكرامية(٢) والحنابلة (۳) الزاعمين أنَّ كلامه تعالى عرَضُ مِنْ جِنسِ الأصواتِ والحروف، إلا أنه قديم قائم بذاته تعالى.
Then speech is not with letters * and not with arrangement like the familiar. And what the Mu'tazila went to of the impossibility of speech for Him, the Exalted, because it only occurs with letters and sounds, and precedence and delay, and other than that, and all these are created, and it is not valid that the Exalted be qualified with created things, otherwise He would be created, and they diverted what came in the Book and the Sunnah, that He the Exalted is speaking, from its apparent meaning to the meaning that He is the Creator of speech in other than Him, like the tree that spoke to Moses, peace be upon him, for example, so speech is an attribute of other than Him, not His attribute, the Exalted. Ahl al-Sunna answered by denying the confinement of speech to letters and sounds, by making speech two types: verbal and internal, and the second is intended, as he indicated by his saying: (Then speech) i.e., His speech, the Exalted, which is an attribute of His essence, is internal, (not with letters) and sounds, (and not) clothed with (arrangement) of precedence and delay, (like) created speech (familiar) to us, and then the impossible does not follow. And in my saying: 'And not with letters... etc.' there is also a refutation of the Karramiyya (2) and the Hanabila (3) who claim that His speech, the Exalted, is an accident of the genus of sounds and letters, except that it is eternal, subsisting in His essence, the Exalted.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage addresses divine speech (الكلام) and refutes the Mu'tazila who deny that God speaks because they confine speech to letters and sounds, which are created. The author explains that the Mu'tazila reinterpret the verses and hadith about God speaking to mean that He creates speech in others (like the tree for Moses). Ahl al-Sunna respond by dividing speech into two kinds: verbal (لفظي) and internal (نفسي). The attribute of God is internal speech, not dependent on letters, sounds, or temporal sequence. This avoids the problem of attributing created things to God. The passage also refutes the Karramiyya and Hanabila (a later group) who claim that God's speech is an accident of sounds and letters but eternal. By affirming that divine speech is internal and not composed of letters or sounds, the impossible consequences are avoided.

Misconception: Some think that God's speech must be like human speech with letters and sounds.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunna affirm that God's speech is an eternal internal attribute without letters, sounds, or temporal sequence, unlike created speech.

Checkpoint
How do Ahl al-Sunna respond to the Mu'tazila's objection that God cannot speak because speech requires letters and sounds?
A) They deny that God speaks at all.
B) They say God's speech is created in a tree.
C) They divide speech into verbal and internal, and affirm that God's speech is internal.
D) They claim God's speech is composed of eternal letters.

Key Takeaway
Allah's speech is an eternal internal attribute, not composed of letters, sounds, or temporal sequence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you ever stop to think that the words you hear are not the actual speech of Allah, but only a created expression of His eternal internal speech? How does that reshape your sense of awe and connection to the Quran?
?
The Mu'tazila rejected divine speech because they only imagined speech as human-like. Are there any attributes of Allah that you unconsciously imagine as similar to human attributes, and what would it cost you to truly affirm His transcendence?
?
If Allah's speech is an eternal inner attribute without letters or sounds, how must He know you and speak to you beyond mere words? Are you listening to that internal address in your soul, or have you been content with only outward recitation?

Divine Attributes

Divine Speech is Mental, Not Verbal
Imam Dardeer defines divine speech as nafsi and rejects letter-composition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sunni theologians distinguish between mental (nafsi) and verbal (lafzi) speech to defend God's attribute of speech.

Core Idea
Divine speech is an eternal mental attribute, not letters or sounds.

This lesson clarifies a crucial point of Islamic theology: what does it mean that God speaks? Some groups concluded that because human speech involves letters and sounds, which are contingent, God cannot truly speak. The Sunni response, as articulated by Imam Dardeer, is to distinguish two types of speech. This passage presents that distinction and uses it to refute both the Mu'tazila and extremists who claimed God's speech is made of letters.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the English translation. Notice the structure: objection, reinterpretation, answer, and additional refutation.
The poem line at the beginning is the core statement.
2
Identify the Mu'tazilite argument
Understand why the Mu'tazila concluded that God cannot speak: because speech consists of letters and sounds, which are contingent. Then see how they reinterpreted verses about God speaking.
3
Learn the Sunni distinction
The Sunni response is to divide speech into two types: lafzi (verbal) and nafsi (mental). Divine speech is the latter, not composed of letters or sounds, so no contingency applies.
This is the key doctrinal point.
4
Notice the additional refutation
The author also uses the same distinction to refute the Karramiyya and certain Hanabila who claimed God's speech is an eternal accident of sounds.
This shows the broad application of the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤٢ - ثُمَّ الكلامُ لَيسَ بالحروفِ * ولَيسَ بالترتيب كالمألوف وما ذهب المعتزلة إلى استحالة الكلامِ عليه تعالى، لأنه إنما يكونُ بحُروفِ وأصوات، وتقديم وتأخير، وغير ذلك، وهذه كلها حادثة، ولا يصح اتصافه تعالى بالحوادث، وإلا لكان حادثا، وصرَفوا ما ورَدَ في الكتاب والسُّنَّةْ، مِنْ أنه تعالى متكلم عن ظاهره، على معنى أنه خالق الكلام في غيره، كالشَّجَرَةِ التي كلّمت موسى العليا مثلا، فالكلامُ صِفةٌ غَيره لا صفَتُه تعالى.. أَجَابَ أَهْلُ السُّنَّةِ بِمَنْعِ حَضْرِ الكَلام في الحروفِ والأصوات، بجعل الكلامِ قسمين: لفظي ونفسي، والثاني هو المراد، كما أشار إليه بقوله: (ثُمَّ الكلام) أي: كلامه تعالى، الذي هو صفةُ ذاتِه، نفْسِي، (لَيسَ بالحروف) والأصوات)، (ولَيسَ) مُتلَبّسا (بالترتيب) مِنْ تقديم وتأخير، (ك) الكلام الحادث (المألوف) لنا، وحينَئِذٍ فلا يلزم المحالُ. وفي قولي: «وليسَ بالحروفِ... إلخ» ردُّ أيضًا على الكرامية(٢) والحنابلة (۳) الزاعمين أنَّ كلامه تعالى عرَضُ مِنْ جِنسِ الأصواتِ والحروف، إلا أنه قديم قائم بذاته تعالى. (۱) لأن الحروف والأصوات أعراض حادثة مشروط حدوث بعضها بانقضاء بعض، لأن امتناع التكلم بالحرف الثاني بدون انقضاء الحرف الأول بديهي. (٢) الكرامية (أصحاب محمد بن كرام فرقة ذهبت إلى التجسيم والتشبيه قالوا: إن كلامه تعالى حادث قائم بذاته لتجويزهم قيام الحوادث بذاته تعالى ومعنى قيام الحوادث أنه يوجد في ذاته تعالى ويقوم بها ما لم يكن من قبل. (۳) ليس المراد بهم أتباع الإمام أحمد ولكنهم طائفة من متأخري الحنابلة زعموا ذلك فشانوا به مذهب الإمام أحمد رض الله وقام ابن الجوزي في دفع شبه التشبيه بالرد عليهم، قالوا: إن كلامه تعالى من جنس الحروف والأصوات إلا أنه قديم.. إلخ
42 - Then speech is not with letters, and not with order like what is familiar. And what the Mu'tazila went to of the impossibility of speech for Him, Most High, because it only occurs with letters and sounds, and precedence and delay, and other than that, and all these are contingent, and it is not valid for Him, Most High, to be described with contingent things, otherwise He would be contingent. And they interpreted what came in the Book and the Sunnah, that He, Most High, is speaking (mutakallim) according to its apparent meaning, to mean that He is the creator of speech in other than Him, like the tree that spoke to Moses, for example, so speech is a description of other than Him, not His description. The Ahl al-Sunnah answered by denying the restriction of speech to letters and sounds, by making speech two types: verbal (lafzi) and mental (nafsi), and the second is what is intended, as indicated by his saying: (Then speech) meaning: His speech, Most High, which is the attribute of His essence, is mental (nafsi), (not with letters and sounds), and (not) clothed (with order) of precedence and delay, (like) contingent speech (familiar) to us, and then the impossible does not follow. And in my saying: 'Not with letters... etc.' is also a reply against the Karramiyya and the Hanabila who claim that His speech, Most High, is an accident of the genus of sounds and letters, except that it is eternal (qadim) subsisting in His essence, Most High. (1) Because letters and sounds are contingent accidents, the occurrence of some being conditioned by the passing of others, because the impossibility of speaking the second letter without the passing of the first is self-evident. (2) The Karramiyya (the followers of Muhammad bin Karram, a sect that went to corporealism and anthropomorphism, said: His speech, Most High, is contingent (hadith) subsisting in His essence, because they permit the occurrence of contingent things in His essence, Most High, and the meaning of the occurrence of contingent things is that He brings into existence in His essence, Most High, and it subsists in Him what was not before. (3) By them is not meant the followers of Imam Ahmad, but rather a group of late Hanabila who claimed that, and thereby defamed the madhhab of Imam Ahmad, may Allah be pleased with him, and Ibn al-Jawzi stood to refute them in his book 'Deflecting the Likeness of Anthropomorphism'. They said: His speech, Most High, is of the genus of letters and sounds except that it is eternal... etc.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument defending the Sunni position on the nature of divine speech. It begins by citing the poem: 'Then speech is not with letters, and not with order like what is familiar.' The commentary then explains the Mu'tazilite objection: they considered speech impossible for God because speech in human experience consists of letters, sounds, and temporal sequence—all contingent. Since God cannot be described with contingent things (otherwise He would be contingent), they reinterpreted scriptural verses about God speaking as meaning God creates speech in other beings (e.g., the tree that spoke to Moses). Thus, for them, speech is an attribute of something else, not of God. The Sunni response, as explained by the author, is to deny that speech is restricted to letters and sounds. Instead, speech is divided into two types: verbal (lafzi) and mental (nafsi). Divine speech is the latter—a mental attribute of God's essence, not composed of letters, sounds, or temporal order. Therefore, the charge of impossibility does not apply. The author then notes that this same division also refutes the claims of the Karramiyya and certain late Hanabila, who asserted that God's speech is an eternal accident of the genus of sounds and letters subsisting in His essence. The footnotes further explain why letters and sounds are contingent (each letter's occurrence depends on the passing of the previous one, self-evidently) and provide background on the Karramiyya and Hanabila positions.

Key Terms
كلام نفسي
كلام لفظي
حروف
أصوات
حادثة
قديم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Divine speech must consist of letters and sounds, just like human speech.
Correction: Divine speech is a mental (nafsi) attribute, not composed of letters or sounds, so it is not contingent.

Checkpoint
According to the Sunni position in this passage, what is the nature of God's speech?
A) It consists of letters and sounds, like human speech.
B) It is a mental (nafsi) attribute not composed of letters or sounds.
C) It is an eternal accident of the genus of sounds.
D) God does not speak; speech is created in others.

Key Takeaway
Divine speech is a mental attribute, not composed of letters or sounds, thus the Mu'tazilite objection fails.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you ever remember that the words you utter are not identical to God's eternal speech? How does that distinction challenge you to approach the Quran with greater awe and humility?
?
The Mu'tazila rejected God's speech because they could not imagine it without letters and sounds. Can you think of any attributes you might be unintentionally limiting to your human experience? What would it mean for your faith to truly affirm that God's attributes are beyond our comprehension?
?
If divine speech is a mental attribute without temporal order, what does that imply about God's knowledge of your past, present, and future? Are you living as if God's word to you is eternal and unchanging, or do you treat it as just another human book?

Divine Attributes
beginner

Introduction to Impossible Attributes: Non-Existence, Origination, Annihilation
Opening enumeration of impossible attributes 1–3.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the first three impossible attributes for Allah are non-existence, origination, and annihilation, which are the opposites of His necessary attributes of existence, pre-eternity, and everlastingness.

Core Idea
Allah's necessary attributes make their opposites impossible.

Imam Dardeer begins by establishing a key principle: the thirteen impossible attributes are the exact opposites of the thirteen necessary attributes. He then lists the first three—non-existence, origination, and annihilation—showing how they contradict Allah's absolute perfection. This lesson introduces the method of negation used in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening principle
Note that Dardeer says the impossible attributes are 'opposites of the attributes' (أضداد الصفات). Understand that what is necessary for Allah cannot be negated.
2
Identify the first three impossible attributes
Find non-existence (العدم), origination (الحدوث), and annihilation (الفناء) in the list. Notice how they correspond to existence, pre-eternity, and everlastingness.
3
Reflect on why these are impossible
Since Allah is necessarily existent, pre-eternal, and everlasting, their negations cannot apply to Him. This is a logical inference from His perfection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي أضداد الصفات
إذا علمت ذلك فيستحيلُ عليه تعالى ثلاث عشرة صفة، و الأولى، لما علمتَ أنها واجبةٌ له تعالى، والواجب لا يقبلُ الانتفاء.
فيستحيل عليه تعالى:
١ - العدم -
٢ - والحدوث،
٣- وطرقُ العدم، ويسمى الفناء،
٤ - والمماثلة للحوادث، مِنْ حِرميّة أو عرَضيّة، أو حلولٍ، أو اتصال أو انفصال، أو بغد أو قُرب، أو كبير أو صغر.
ه - وكذا يستحيلُ عليه تعالى عدَمُ القيام بالنفْسِ، بأنْ يفْتَقِرَ إلى محل أو مُخَصِّص.
٦ - وعدم الوحدانية، بأنْ يكونَ ذا كثرة في ذاته أو صفاته، أو يكون له شريكٌ فِي فِعلٍ مِنَ الْأَفْعَالِ.
- وكذا يستحيل عليه تعالى الجهل، مُرَكَّبًا أو بسيطًا، أو ما في معناه: مِنْ ظَنِّ أو غفلة أو نِسْيان أو نوم أو اشتغال بشأن عنْ شأْن.
۸- ويستحيل عليه تعالى الموتُ
٩ - والعجز، وما في معناه: مِنْ فُتور أو نصب
١٠ - والكراهية، أي: عدَمُ الإرادة، بأن يقع في مُلْكِه ما لا يُريدُه، أو تصدرَ الكائنات عنه تعالى بالتعليل أو بالطبع؛ لما يـ[؟] مِنْ قِدَمِ العالَم، الذي قامَ البُرْهانُ القاطع على حُدوثِه، ووَرَدَ الشرع به لأنه يجب اقتران العلة بمعلولها، والطبيعة بمطبوعها، والقائل بذلك كافر بإجماع المسلمين كما تقدم. وتقدَّمَ الفَرقُ بَينَ الفاعِلِ بالعِلةِ والفاعل بالطبع: مِنْ أَنَّ العِلَّةَ لا تتوقَّفُ على وُجود شَرط ولا انتفاء مانع، والطبيعة تتوقَّفُ على ذلك. وتما يَدُلُّ على بطلانها اختلاف أنواع العالم على كثرتها، إِذْ مَعْلُولُ العِلةِ والطبيعة لا يختلفُ.
١١ - وكذا يستحيل عليه تعالى البَكُمُ، أَيْ: عدَمُ الكَلامِ بُوجودِ آفةٍ تمنعُ مِنه، وفي معناه الشكوتُ النَّفْسيه [؟].
١٢، ١٣ - ويستحيل عليه تعالى الصَّمَمُ والعمى، تعالى الله عن ذلك عُلُوًّا كبيرًا.
And they are the opposites of the attributes. When you know that, then it is impossible for Him, exalted, [to have] thirteen attributes, and the first, because you know they are necessary for Him, exalted, and the necessary does not accept negation. So it is impossible for Him, exalted: 1 - Non-existence, 2 - Origination, 3 - The approach of non-existence, called annihilation, 4 - Likeness to originated things, whether in essence or accident, or indwelling, or connection or separation, or distance or nearness, or bigness or smallness. 5 - Likewise impossible for Him, exalted, is not being self-subsistent, by being in need of a place or a particularizer. 6 - And lack of oneness, by being multiple in His essence or attributes, or having a partner in any of the acts. 7 - And likewise impossible for Him, exalted, is ignorance, compound or simple, or what is in its meaning: conjecture, heedlessness, forgetfulness, sleep, or preoccupation with one matter over another. 8 - And it is impossible for Him, exalted, death. 9 - And incapability, and what is in its meaning: languor or fatigue. 10 - And aversion, meaning lack of will, such that something occurs in His dominion that He does not will, or that beings proceed from Him, exalted, by causation or by nature; because of [what follows?] from the eternity of the world, which the decisive proof has established as originated, and the Revealed Law has come with it, because the cause must be accompanied by its effect, and the nature by its natural thing, and the one who says that is a disbeliever by consensus of the Muslims as has preceded. And the distinction between the agent by cause and the agent by nature has preceded: that the cause does not depend on the existence of a condition nor the absence of an obstacle, while nature depends on that. And that which indicates its falsity is the variation of the types of the world despite their abundance, since the effect of the cause and nature does not vary. 11 - And likewise impossible for Him, exalted, is muteness, meaning lack of speech due to an impediment preventing it, and in its meaning is inner silence [؟]. 12, 13 - And it is impossible for Him, exalted, deafness and blindness, exalted is Allah above that with a great exaltation.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation of the thirteen attributes that are impossible for Allah, as the opposites of the necessary attributes. The author begins by stating that these are the opposites (أضداد) of the attributes (presumably the divine attributes). He reminds the reader that since the necessary attributes are necessary for Allah, they cannot be negated; thus their opposites are impossible. Then he enumerates them sequentially, each with a brief explanation of what it means.

1. Non-existence (العدم): the opposite of existence.
2. Origination (الحدوث): the opposite of pre-eternity.
3. The approach of non-existence (طرق العدم) called annihilation (الفناء): this is the opposite of everlastingness.
4. Likeness to created things (المماثلة للحوادث): includes similarity in essence or accident, indwelling (حلول), connection or separation, distance or nearness, bigness or smallness. This is the opposite of being unlike anything.
5. Not being self-subsistent (عدم القيام بالنفس): i.e., needing a place or a particularizer (مخصِّص). This is the opposite of being self-subsistent.
6. Lack of oneness (عدم الوحدانية): meaning multiplicity in essence or attributes, or having a partner in any act. This is the opposite of oneness.
7. Ignorance (الجهل): compound or simple, or anything similar like conjecture, heedlessness, forgetfulness, sleep, or distraction. This is the opposite of knowledge.
8. Death (الموت): the opposite of life.
9. Incapability (العجز): including languor (فتور) and fatigue (نصب). Opposite of power.
10. Aversion (الكراهية): i.e., lack of will (عدم الإرادة). The author explains that this would mean something occurs in His dominion that He does not will, or that beings proceed from Him by causation (التعليل) or by nature (الطبع). He links this to the issue of the eternity of the world, which has been refuted by proof and revelation. He also distinguishes between an agent by cause and an agent by nature: the cause does not depend on conditions or absence of obstacles, while nature does. The variation among worldly things disproves causation/nature, because their effects would not vary.
11. Muteness (البكم): lack of speech due to an impediment. The author adds 'inner silence' (الشكوت النفسيه? unclear).
12 & 13. Deafness (الصمم) and blindness (العمى): both impossible for Allah. The passage ends with an exaltation: 'exalted is Allah above that with a great exaltation.'

The author's method is to list each impossible attribute as the negation of a necessary attribute, and to provide a concise definition or explanation that clarifies what is being negated. Some entries include arguments against those who might affirm such attributes for Allah (e.g., the refutation of causality in item 10).

Key Terms
العدم
الحدوث
الفناء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that only necessary attributes matter for understanding Allah.
Correction: This passage shows that knowing what is impossible for Allah is equally important for tawheed.

Checkpoint
What is the relationship between the impossible attributes and the necessary attributes?
A) They are identical.
B) They are opposites.
C) They have no relation.
D) They are unrelated.

Key Takeaway
The first three impossible attributes—non-existence, origination, and annihilation—directly negate Allah's necessary attributes of existence, pre-eternity, and everlastingness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson teaches that non-existence is impossible for Allah. In your own life, where do you act as if Allah might 'fail' or 'cease' to exist—perhaps by placing ultimate trust in people or things? How would your daily choices change if you truly lived knowing Allah's existence is absolutely necessary and cannot cease?
?
Origination (having a beginning) is impossible for Allah. Yet you may treat some of your struggles as if they have no end, forgetting that only Allah is pre-eternal and everlasting. What current difficulty would be transformed if you centered it on the reality that Allah alone has no beginning and no end?

Divine Attributes

Impossible Attribute of Likeness to Created Things
Enumeration and explanation of the fourth impossible attribute: likeness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah cannot be like any created thing in any respect, whether in essence, accident, or relational aspects.

Core Idea
Allah is utterly unlike everything else.

The fourth impossible attribute is likeness (المماثلة) to created things. Imam Dardeer specifies that this includes similarity in essence or accident, as well as relational categories like connection, separation, distance, and size. This lesson emphasizes Allah's utter transcendence beyond any comparison.

Guided Path
1
Read the fourth impossible attribute
Find the entry for number 4 in the Arabic passage. Note the specific categories listed: essence, accident, indwelling, connection, etc.
2
Understand the scope of 'likeness'
Likeness is not limited to physical similarity; it includes any comparison in attributes or relationships. Allah is beyond all categories of created things.
3
Reflect on the principle of 'laythu kamithlihi shay'
This verse (42:11) supports the impossibility of likeness. Dardeer's enumeration shows the logical extension of this principle.

?

Divine Attributes

Impossible Attributes of Self‑Subsistence and Oneness
Enumeration and explanation of impossible attributes 5 and 6.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah cannot be dependent on a place or a particularizer, nor can He be multiple in essence, attributes, or have a partner in acts.

Core Idea
Allah is self‑subsistent and absolutely one.

Imam Dardeer continues with two more impossible attributes: not being self‑subsistent (i.e., needing a place or specific determiner) and lacking oneness (i.e., having multiplicity or a partner). These negations protect the core Islamic beliefs in Allah's independence and tawheed.

Guided Path
1
Read the fifth impossible attribute
Find 'عدم القيام بالنفس' and understand that it means Allah is not dependent on anything external, like a location or a particularizer.
2
Read the sixth impossible attribute
Find 'عدم الوحدانية' and note that it denies any form of multiplicity in Allah's essence, attributes, or acts.
3
Connect to core tenets
These two attributes directly affirm Allah's self‑sufficiency (ghina) and His oneness (tawheed).

2. Origination (الحدوث): the opposite of pre-eternity.
3. The approach of non-existence (طرق العدم) called annihilation (الفناء): this is the opposite of everlastingness.
4. Likeness to created things (المماثلة للحوادث): includes similarity in essence or accident, indwelling (حلول), connection or separation, distance or nearness, bigness or smallness. This is the opposite of being unlike anything.
5. Not being self-subsistent (عدم القيام بالنفس): i.e., needing a place or a particularizer (مخصِّص). This is the opposite of being self-subsistent.
6. Lack of oneness (عدم الوحدانية): meaning multiplicity in essence or attributes, or having a partner in any act. This is the opposite of oneness.
7. Ignorance (الجهل): compound or simple, or anything similar like conjecture, heedlessness, forgetfulness, sleep, or distraction. This is the opposite of knowledge.
8. Death (الموت): the opposite of life.
9. Incapability (العجز): including languor (فتور) and fatigue (نصب). Opposite of power.
10. Aversion (الكراهية): i.e., lack of will (عدم الإرادة). The author explains that this would mean something occurs in His dominion that He does not will, or that beings proceed from Him by causation (التعليل) or by nature (الطبع). He links this to the issue of the eternity of the world, which has been refuted by proof and revelation. He also distinguishes between an agent by cause and an agent by nature: the cause does not depend on conditions or absence of obstacles, while nature does. The variation among worldly things disproves causation/nature, because their effects would not vary.
11. Muteness (البكم): lack of speech due to an impediment. The author adds 'inner silence' (الشكوت النفسيه? unclear).
12 & 13. Deafness (الصمم) and blindness (العمى): both impossible for Allah. The passage ends with an exaltation: 'exalted is Allah above that with a great exaltation.'

The author's method is to list each impossible attribute as the negation of a necessary attribute, and to provide a concise definition or explanation that clarifies what is being negated. Some entries include arguments against those who might affirm such attributes for Allah (e.g., the refutation of causality in item 10).

Key Terms
القيام بالنفس
الوحدانية
مُخَصِّص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does 'عدم القيام بالنفس' mean?
A) Not having a body
B) Not needing a place or particularizer
C) Not having partners
D) Not having attributes

Key Takeaway
Allah is self‑subsistent and absolutely one; He depends on nothing and has no partner.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah is completely self-sufficient and needs nothing, why do you constantly rely on created things for your security and happiness? Today, identify one thing you depend on more than Allah and consciously turn to Him first.
?
Do you truly believe that Allah alone controls all outcomes, or do you sometimes act as if someone else has the final say over your life? Recall a time you feared a creation more than the Creator; what would it take to replace that fear with reliance on Allah alone?
?
The passage says Allah cannot have a partner in any act. Is there any area of your life—like your career, relationships, or worries—where you attribute outcomes to factors other than Allah? Commit to adjusting your mindset to see only His hand in every result.
