Impossible Attributes of Ignorance, Death, and Incapability
Enumeration and explanation of impossible attributes 7‑9.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah cannot possess ignorance, death, or incapability, and that these negate His necessary attributes of knowledge, life, and power.

Core Idea
Allah is all‑knowing, ever‑living, and all‑powerful.

Imam Dardeer lists three more impossible attributes: ignorance, death, and incapability. These are the direct opposites of Allah's necessary attributes of knowledge, life, and power. The author also includes related concepts to ensure complete negation.

Guided Path
1
Read the seventh impossible attribute
Find 'الجهل' and note the various forms: compound, simple, conjecture, heedlessness, etc.
2
Read the eighth and ninth impossible attributes
Find 'الموت' and 'العجز' and their related meanings: languor, fatigue.
3
Understand the pattern of negation
Each impossible attribute negates a kind of imperfection that cannot apply to Allah. Together they affirm His absolute perfection in knowledge, life, and power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي أضداد الصفات
إذا علمت ذلك فيستحيلُ عليه تعالى ثلاث عشرة صفة، و الأولى، لما علمتَ أنها واجبةٌ له تعالى، والواجب لا يقبلُ الانتفاء.
فيستحيل عليه تعالى:
١ - العدم -
٢ - والحدوث،
٣- وطرقُ العدم، ويسمى الفناء،
٤ - والمماثلة للحوادث، مِنْ حِرميّة أو عرَضيّة، أو حلولٍ، أو اتصال أو انفصال، أو بغد أو قُرب، أو كبير أو صغر.
ه - وكذا يستحيلُ عليه تعالى عدَمُ القيام بالنفْسِ، بأنْ يفْتَقِرَ إلى محل أو مُخَصِّص.
٦ - وعدم الوحدانية، بأنْ يكونَ ذا كثرة في ذاته أو صفاته، أو يكون له شريكٌ فِي فِعلٍ مِنَ الْأَفْعَالِ.
- وكذا يستحيل عليه تعالى الجهل، مُرَكَّبًا أو بسيطًا، أو ما في معناه: مِنْ ظَنِّ أو غفلة أو نِسْيان أو نوم أو اشتغال بشأن عنْ شأْن.
۸- ويستحيل عليه تعالى الموتُ
٩ - والعجز، وما في معناه: مِنْ فُتور أو نصب
١٠ - والكراهية، أي: عدَمُ الإرادة، بأن يقع في مُلْكِه ما لا يُريدُه، أو تصدرَ الكائنات عنه تعالى بالتعليل أو بالطبع؛ لما يـ[؟] مِنْ قِدَمِ العالَم، الذي قامَ البُرْهانُ القاطع على حُدوثِه، ووَرَدَ الشرع به لأنه يجب اقتران العلة بمعلولها، والطبيعة بمطبوعها، والقائل بذلك كافر بإجماع المسلمين كما تقدم. وتقدَّمَ الفَرقُ بَينَ الفاعِلِ بالعِلةِ والفاعل بالطبع: مِنْ أَنَّ العِلَّةَ لا تتوقَّفُ على وُجود شَرط ولا انتفاء مانع، والطبيعة تتوقَّفُ على ذلك. وتما يَدُلُّ على بطلانها اختلاف أنواع العالم على كثرتها، إِذْ مَعْلُولُ العِلةِ والطبيعة لا يختلفُ.
١١ - وكذا يستحيل عليه تعالى البَكُمُ، أَيْ: عدَمُ الكَلامِ بُوجودِ آفةٍ تمنعُ مِنه، وفي معناه الشكوتُ النَّفْسيه [؟].
١٢، ١٣ - ويستحيل عليه تعالى الصَّمَمُ والعمى، تعالى الله عن ذلك عُلُوًّا كبيرًا.
And they are the opposites of the attributes. When you know that, then it is impossible for Him, exalted, [to have] thirteen attributes, and the first, because you know they are necessary for Him, exalted, and the necessary does not accept negation. So it is impossible for Him, exalted: 1 - Non-existence, 2 - Origination, 3 - The approach of non-existence, called annihilation, 4 - Likeness to originated things, whether in essence or accident, or indwelling, or connection or separation, or distance or nearness, or bigness or smallness. 5 - Likewise impossible for Him, exalted, is not being self-subsistent, by being in need of a place or a particularizer. 6 - And lack of oneness, by being multiple in His essence or attributes, or having a partner in any of the acts. 7 - And likewise impossible for Him, exalted, is ignorance, compound or simple, or what is in its meaning: conjecture, heedlessness, forgetfulness, sleep, or preoccupation with one matter over another. 8 - And it is impossible for Him, exalted, death. 9 - And incapability, and what is in its meaning: languor or fatigue. 10 - And aversion, meaning lack of will, such that something occurs in His dominion that He does not will, or that beings proceed from Him, exalted, by causation or by nature; because of [what follows?] from the eternity of the world, which the decisive proof has established as originated, and the Revealed Law has come with it, because the cause must be accompanied by its effect, and the nature by its natural thing, and the one who says that is a disbeliever by consensus of the Muslims as has preceded. And the distinction between the agent by cause and the agent by nature has preceded: that the cause does not depend on the existence of a condition nor the absence of an obstacle, while nature depends on that. And that which indicates its falsity is the variation of the types of the world despite their abundance, since the effect of the cause and nature does not vary. 11 - And likewise impossible for Him, exalted, is muteness, meaning lack of speech due to an impediment preventing it, and in its meaning is inner silence [؟]. 12, 13 - And it is impossible for Him, exalted, deafness and blindness, exalted is Allah above that with a great exaltation.

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation of the thirteen attributes that are impossible for Allah, as the opposites of the necessary attributes. The author begins by stating that these are the opposites (أضداد) of the attributes (presumably the divine attributes). He reminds the reader that since the necessary attributes are necessary for Allah, they cannot be negated; thus their opposites are impossible. Then he enumerates them sequentially, each with a brief explanation of what it means.

1. Non-existence (العدم): the opposite of existence.
2. Origination (الحدوث): the opposite of pre-eternity.
3. The approach of non-existence (طرق العدم) called annihilation (الفناء): this is the opposite of everlastingness.
4. Likeness to created things (المماثلة للحوادث): includes similarity in essence or accident, indwelling (حلول), connection or separation, distance or nearness, bigness or smallness. This is the opposite of being unlike anything.
5. Not being self-subsistent (عدم القيام بالنفس): i.e., needing a place or a particularizer (مخصِّص). This is the opposite of being self-subsistent.
6. Lack of oneness (عدم الوحدانية): meaning multiplicity in essence or attributes, or having a partner in any act. This is the opposite of oneness.
7. Ignorance (الجهل): compound or simple, or anything similar like conjecture, heedlessness, forgetfulness, sleep, or distraction. This is the opposite of knowledge.
8. Death (الموت): the opposite of life.
9. Incapability (العجز): including languor (فتور) and fatigue (نصب). Opposite of power.
10. Aversion (الكراهية): i.e., lack of will (عدم الإرادة). The author explains that this would mean something occurs in His dominion that He does not will, or that beings proceed from Him by causation (التعليل) or by nature (الطبع). He links this to the issue of the eternity of the world, which has been refuted by proof and revelation. He also distinguishes between an agent by cause and an agent by nature: the cause does not depend on conditions or absence of obstacles, while nature does. The variation among worldly things disproves causation/nature, because their effects would not vary.
11. Muteness (البكم): lack of speech due to an impediment. The author adds 'inner silence' (الشكوت النفسيه? unclear).
12 & 13. Deafness (الصمم) and blindness (العمى): both impossible for Allah. The passage ends with an exaltation: 'exalted is Allah above that with a great exaltation.'

The author's method is to list each impossible attribute as the negation of a necessary attribute, and to provide a concise definition or explanation that clarifies what is being negated. Some entries include arguments against those who might affirm such attributes for Allah (e.g., the refutation of causality in item 10).

?

?
Are there areas of your life where you act as if your own capability is enough, forgetting that Allah's power is absolute? What is one thing you are holding onto as if you are in control? Surrender it to Allah right now, even if just in your heart.
?
If Allah were subject to death or fatigue, how would your trust in Him be shaken? Since He is not, what fear or worry can you release today, knowing His life and power are eternal and unfailing?

Impossible Attribute of Aversion: Refuting Causality and Nature
Enumeration and argument for the tenth impossible attribute: aversion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah cannot have aversion (lack of will), and that this includes refuting the idea that events proceed from Him by necessary causation or nature.

Core Idea
Allah's will is absolute; nothing occurs without His will.

The tenth impossible attribute is aversion (الكراهية), defined as lack of will. Imam Dardeer explains that this would mean something occurs in Allah's dominion that He does not will, or that creation proceeds from Him by causation or nature. He then refutes these ideas with rational and scriptural arguments, making this a longer and more theologically significant entry.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of aversion
Find 'الكراهية' and note that it means lack of will (عدم الإرادة). The passage gives two scenarios that would imply this.
2
Understand the two implications
First, something occurring in His dominion against His will. Second, creation proceeding by causation or nature. Both are negated.
3
Study the refutation of causation and nature
The author argues that the eternity of the world is false, and that causation/nature would imply uniformity, which contradicts the variety in the world.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Allah creates through secondary causes or nature, diminishing His will.
Correction: This passage asserts that all events are directly willed by Allah; causation and nature are false doctrines that imply aversion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When something goes wrong in your life, do you instinctively look for 'natural causes' or 'circumstances' rather than seeing Allah's wisdom and will behind it? Are you willing to say, 'This is from Allah' even when you don't understand the reason?
?
If you truly believed that nothing happens without Allah's will, would you still complain about your situation? What would change in your du'ā and your patience if you internalized this truth?
?
Do you ever treat Allah like a 'cause' or 'nature' — expecting a guaranteed outcome from your acts of worship, as if He owes you a result? How can you repent from this subtle idolatry and submit to His absolute will?

Impossible Attributes of Muteness, Deafness, and Blindness
Enumeration of impossible attributes 11‑13: muteness, deafness, blindness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah cannot have muteness, deafness, or blindness, which negate His necessary attributes of speech, hearing, and sight.

Core Idea
Allah speaks, hears, and sees perfectly.

The final three impossible attributes are muteness, deafness, and blindness. Imam Dardeer explains muteness as the lack of speech due to an impediment, and lists deafness and blindness together. These negations affirm that Allah possesses perfect speech, hearing, and sight without any deficiency.

Guided Path
1
Read the eleventh impossible attribute
Find 'البكم' and note that it means lack of speech due to an impediment. The author also mentions 'inner silence' (الشكوت النفسية) if uncertain.
2
Read the twelfth and thirteenth impossible attributes
Deafness and blindness are paired. They negate the possibility that Allah lacks hearing or sight.
3
Reflect on the final exaltation
The passage ends with 'تعالى الله عن ذلك علوًا كبيرًا' emphasizing transcendence.

ه - وكذا يستحيلُ عليه تعالى عدَمُ القيام بالنفْسِ، بأنْ يفْتَقِرَ إلى محل أو مُخَصِّص.
٦ - وعدم الوحدانية، بأنْ يكونَ ذا كثرة في ذاته أو صفاته، أو يكون له شريكٌ فِي فِعلٍ مِنَ الْأَفْعَالِ.
- وكذا يستحيل عليه تعالى الجهل، مُرَكَّبًا أو بسيطًا، أو ما في معناه: مِنْ ظَنِّ أو غفلة أو نِسْيان أو نوم أو اشتغال بشأن عنْ شأْن.
۸- ويستحيل عليه تعالى الموتُ
٩ - والعجز، وما في معناه: مِنْ فُتور أو نصب
١٠ - والكراهية، أي: عدَمُ الإرادة، بأن يقع في مُلْكِه ما لا يُريدُه، أو تصدرَ الكائنات عنه تعالى بالتعليل أو بالطبع؛ لما يـ[؟] مِنْ قِدَمِ العالَم، الذي قامَ البُرْهانُ القاطع على حُدوثِه، ووَرَدَ الشرع به لأنه يجب اقتران العلة بمعلولها، والطبيعة بمطبوعها، والقائل بذلك كافر بإجماع المسلمين كما تقدم. وتقدَّمَ الفَرقُ بَينَ الفاعِلِ بالعِلةِ والفاعل بالطبع: مِنْ أَنَّ العِلَّةَ لا تتوقَّفُ على وُجود شَرط ولا انتفاء مانع، والطبيعة تتوقَّفُ على ذلك. وتما يَدُلُّ على بطلانها اختلاف أنواع العالم على كثرتها، إِذْ مَعْلُولُ العِلةِ والطبيعة لا يختلفُ.
١١ - وكذا يستحيل عليه تعالى البَكُمُ، أَيْ: عدَمُ الكَلامِ بُوجودِ آفةٍ تمنعُ مِنه، وفي معناه الشكوتُ النَّفْسيه [؟].
١٢، ١٣ - ويستحيل عليه تعالى الصَّمَمُ والعمى، تعالى الله عن ذلك عُلُوًّا كبيرًا.
And they are the opposites of the attributes. When you know that, then it is impossible for Him, exalted, [to have] thirteen attributes, and the first, because you know they are necessary for Him, exalted, and the necessary does not accept negation. So it is impossible for Him, exalted: 1 - Non-existence, 2 - Origination, 3 - The approach of non-existence, called annihilation, 4 - Likeness to originated things, whether in essence or accident, or indwelling, or connection or separation, or distance or nearness, or bigness or smallness. 5 - Likewise impossible for Him, exalted, is not being self-subsistent, by being in need of a place or a particularizer. 6 - And lack of oneness, by being multiple in His essence or attributes, or having a partner in any of the acts. 7 - And likewise impossible for Him, exalted, is ignorance, compound or simple, or what is in its meaning: conjecture, heedlessness, forgetfulness, sleep, or preoccupation with one matter over another. 8 - And it is impossible for Him, exalted, death. 9 - And incapability, and what is in its meaning: languor or fatigue. 10 - And aversion, meaning lack of will, such that something occurs in His dominion that He does not will, or that beings proceed from Him, exalted, by causation or by nature; because of [what follows?] from the eternity of the world, which the decisive proof has established as originated, and the Revealed Law has come with it, because the cause must be accompanied by its effect, and the nature by its natural thing, and the one who says that is a disbeliever by consensus of the Muslims as has preceded. And the distinction between the agent by cause and the agent by nature has preceded: that the cause does not depend on the existence of a condition nor the absence of an obstacle, while nature depends on that. And that which indicates its falsity is the variation of the types of the world despite their abundance, since the effect of the cause and nature does not vary. 11 - And likewise impossible for Him, exalted, is muteness, meaning lack of speech due to an impediment preventing it, and in its meaning is inner silence [؟]. 12, 13 - And it is impossible for Him, exalted, deafness and blindness, exalted is Allah above that with a great exaltation.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation of the thirteen attributes that are impossible for Allah, as the opposites of the necessary attributes. The author begins by stating that these are the opposites (أضداد) of the attributes (presumably the divine attributes). He reminds the reader that since the necessary attributes are necessary for Allah, they cannot be negated; thus their opposites are impossible. Then he enumerates them sequentially, each with a brief explanation of what it means.

1. Non-existence (العدم): the opposite of existence.
2. Origination (الحدوث): the opposite of pre-eternity.
3. The approach of non-existence (طرق العدم) called annihilation (الفناء): this is the opposite of everlastingness.
4. Likeness to created things (المماثلة للحوادث): includes similarity in essence or accident, indwelling (حلول), connection or separation, distance or nearness, bigness or smallness. This is the opposite of being unlike anything.
5. Not being self-subsistent (عدم القيام بالنفس): i.e., needing a place or a particularizer (مخصِّص). This is the opposite of being self-subsistent.
6. Lack of oneness (عدم الوحدانية): meaning multiplicity in essence or attributes, or having a partner in any act. This is the opposite of oneness.
7. Ignorance (الجهل): compound or simple, or anything similar like conjecture, heedlessness, forgetfulness, sleep, or distraction. This is the opposite of knowledge.
8. Death (الموت): the opposite of life.
9. Incapability (العجز): including languor (فتور) and fatigue (نصب). Opposite of power.
10. Aversion (الكراهية): i.e., lack of will (عدم الإرادة). The author explains that this would mean something occurs in His dominion that He does not will, or that beings proceed from Him by causation (التعليل) or by nature (الطبع). He links this to the issue of the eternity of the world, which has been refuted by proof and revelation. He also distinguishes between an agent by cause and an agent by nature: the cause does not depend on conditions or absence of obstacles, while nature does. The variation among worldly things disproves causation/nature, because their effects would not vary.
11. Muteness (البكم): lack of speech due to an impediment. The author adds 'inner silence' (الشكوت النفسيه? unclear).
12 & 13. Deafness (الصمم) and blindness (العمى): both impossible for Allah. The passage ends with an exaltation: 'exalted is Allah above that with a great exaltation.'

The author's method is to list each impossible attribute as the negation of a necessary attribute, and to provide a concise definition or explanation that clarifies what is being negated. Some entries include arguments against those who might affirm such attributes for Allah (e.g., the refutation of causality in item 10).

Key Terms
البكم
الصمم
العمى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Allah is free from muteness, deafness, and blindness, affirming His perfect speech, hearing, and sight.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

How often do you call upon Allah without truly believing that He hears every word you utter, even the silent cries of your heart? Today, start each prayer with the firm conviction that as-Sami‘ is listening, and let that transform your khushu‘.
?
Your tongue sometimes describes Allah in ways that mirror human limitations — for example, when you say 'He doesn't care' or 'He is far away.' This lesson shows those thoughts are forms of imputing deficiency. What specific statement will you catch yourself saying and replace with praise befitting Him?
?
You hide your sins from people, but do you forget that al-Basir sees everything? If you truly believed His sight is perfect and unimpaired, would you still commit that sin in private? What step will you take today to act on that awareness?

Proof of Necessary Attributes from Poverty and Worship
Dardeer proves necessary attributes via opposites leading to poverty and contingency, impossible for the worshipped.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Dardeer proves that God must possess essential attributes because lacking them would entail opposites that imply poverty and contingency, contradicting His status as the worshipped Self-Sufficient.

Core Idea
If God lacked an attribute, He would have its opposite, leading to poverty and contingency, impossible for the worshipped.

This passage presents a concise logical proof for the necessity of divine attributes. Dardeer argues that if God were not described with attributes like life, knowledge, and power, He would necessarily be described with their opposites—death, ignorance, incapacity, etc. But those opposites entail need and temporal origination, which are impossible for the One who is worshipped and needs nothing. This argument grounds the essential attributes in God's very nature as the self-sufficient object of worship.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to understand the structure of the argument. Pay attention to the connecting particles like 'li-anna' (because) and 'wa' for circumstantial clauses.
The passage integrates commentary on poetic lines; note how the commentary expands the proof.
2
Identify the key premise
The first premise: If God were not described with the essential attributes (life, knowledge, etc.), then He would be described with their opposites (death, ignorance, etc.). This is based on the logical principle that for any pair of opposites, one must apply.
This relies on the classification of attributes into essential and their opposites.
3
Trace the consequence of opposites
The opposites entail 'poverty' (need for a perfecter) and 'temporal origination' (contingency). The commentary explains that this would make God part of the contingent world, which is impossible.
Imam Dardeer cites a poetic line: 'whoever has other than them is at the utmost poverty.'
4
Understand the proof from worship
The argument concludes by linking to God's being 'the One worshipped.' The phrase 'al-wahid al-ma'bood' is a circumstantial clause meaning 'while being the worshipped One.' Since the worshipped One does not need others, He cannot be poor or contingent.
This shows that worship implies self-sufficiency, reinforcing the impossibility of opposites.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإِنَّما وجبَتْ له هذه الصفاتُ، واستحال عليه أضدادها (لأنه) تعالى (لو لم يكُنْ مَوصوفا بها لكانَ بالسِّوى) أي: بسواها مِنَ الجهل والعجْزِ وغَيرهما ما تقدَّم مِنَ المُستحيلات (معروفا) يعني: موصوفًا. أي أنه لو لم يكنْ مُتَّصِفًا بها لاتَّصَفَ بأضدادها، لكن اتصافه تعالى بأضدادها باطِلٌ لِما يَلْزَمُ عليه مِنَ الافتقار والحدوث، كما أشار إليه بقوله: (وكُلُّ مَنْ قامَ به سواها) أَيْ: غَيْرُها مِنَ الجهل، أو ما في معناه، أو العجز .. إلى آخر الأضداد، (فهو الذي في الفقر) أي: الاحتياج إلى مَنْ يُكَمِّله، وهو مُتعَلَّقٌ بقوله: (قد تناهى) أي: بلَغَ النهايةَ في الفقر، وهو مُحالٌ لأنه يؤدّي إلى الحدوثِ، فيكونُ مِنْ جُملة العالم الحادِثِ المُفْتَقِرِ. والواو في قولنا: (والواحد المعبود) للحال، (لا يفْتَقِرُ لغَيره)، وهو في المعنى دليلٌ لقولنا : «وكلٌّ مَنْ قامَ به... إلخ» لأنه في قَوْةِ قَولِنا: «لأنه معبود، وكُلُّ معبودٍ لا يفتقر».
And indeed these attributes are necessarily incumbent upon Him, and their opposites are impossible for Him, because He, exalted, if He were not described with them, He would be known by other than them, i.e., by other than them such as ignorance and incapacity and others of the previously mentioned impossible things, meaning described. That is, if He were not qualified with them, He would be qualified with their opposites, but His being qualified, exalted, with their opposites is invalid because of what would necessarily follow from them of poverty and temporal origination, as He indicated by His saying: (And everyone in whom other than them resides) i.e., other than them such as ignorance, or what is in its meaning, or incapacity... up to the rest of the opposites, (he is the one who in poverty) i.e., need for someone to perfect him, and it is connected to His saying: (has reached the utmost) i.e., reached the extreme in poverty, and that is impossible because it leads to temporal origination, so he becomes part of the contingent world that is in need. And the waw in our saying: (And the One, the worshipped) is for the state, (does not need other than Him), and it is in meaning a proof for our saying: 'And everyone in whom other than them resides...' because it is in the force of our saying: 'Because He is worshipped, and every worshipped does not need.'
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage provides a proof that God must have essential attributes (like life, knowledge, power, will, hearing, sight, speech) and that their opposites (death, ignorance, incapacity, etc.) are impossible. The argument proceeds: If God were not described with these attributes, then He would be described with their opposites (since something must be either knowing or ignorant, etc.). But being described with opposites entails poverty (need for a perfecter) and temporal origination (contingency), which are impossible for God because He is the worshipped One who needs nothing. The author cites the poetic line (line 44) as support: 'because if He were not described with them, He would be known by other than them.' Then line 45: 'whoever has other than them is at the utmost poverty.' Line 46: 'the One worshipped does not need other than Him.' The commentary explains that the waw in 'wal-wahid al-ma'bood' is a waw of state, and the phrase serves as a proof for the preceding statement, since it is equivalent to saying 'because He is worshipped, and every worshipped does not need.' Thus the impossibility of opposites is grounded in God's being the object of worship, which implies self-sufficiency.

Key Terms
الصفات
الأضداد
الافتقار
الحدوث
الواحد المعبود
الفقر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is possible for God to simply lack an attribute without having its opposite; for example, not being knowledgeable does not imply ignorance.
Correction: The logical principle of exhaustive opposites: for essential attributes like knowledge and ignorance, one must exist if the subject is capable of knowledge. Since God is living and rational, absence of knowledge would necessarily imply ignorance. Thus lacking an attribute entails its opposite.

Checkpoint
According to the proof, why is it impossible for God to be described with the opposites of the essential attributes?
A) Because it would entail that He is poor and contingent
B) Because He is naturally good
C) Because the attributes are eternal
D) Because He is worshipped, which requires wealth

Key Takeaway
God must possess all essential attributes because lacking one would imply its opposite, which leads to poverty and contingency—impossible for the self-sufficient worshipped One.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

How does this lesson's proof that He is absolutely self-sufficient challenge your hidden assumptions about your relationship with Him? What would change in your prayer if you believed this with full certainty?
?
If you were to neglect one of God's attributes in your heart—say, His all-encompassing knowledge—what opposite are you implicitly attributing to Him? And what does that reveal about your own need to feel hidden from Him? This week, what is one specific area of your life where you can act on the belief that He possesses all attributes perfectly and needs nothing?
?
The proof says that lacking an attribute leads to poverty and contingency. God as the worshipped One cannot be poor. When you worship, do you feel that God is complete in Himself or that He depends on your worship? Commit today to one concrete thought or action that reminds you of His utter independence.

The Necessity of Divine Attributes and Impossibility of Their Opposites
Dardeer proves the necessity of divine attributes via the impossibility of their opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof for why God's attributes of meanings are necessary and why their opposites are impossible.

Core Idea
If God lacked perfect attributes, He would have imperfect opposites—impossible due to need and temporality.

This lesson presents a concise proof from Imam Dardeer showing that certain perfect attributes are necessarily true of God. The argument rests on a simple but powerful logical step: the absence of a necessary perfection implies the presence of its opposite, which leads to imperfection and contingency. As you read the passage, notice how the author moves from the necessity of attributes to the impossibility of their opposites.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the two lines of verse (44-45) and their translation. Then read the commentary that follows, which unpacks the logical argument.
2
Identify the logical structure
Notice the conditional reasoning: if not described with these attributes, then described with opposites. Then note why those opposites are impossible (need and temporality).
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this proof establishes necessity for the attributes. How does the impossibility of the opposite force the attributes to be necessary?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٤٤ - لأنه لو لم يكُنْ مَوصوفا * بها لكانَ بالسوى معروفا
٤٥ - وكُلَّ مَنْ قامَ بهِ سِواها * فهو الذي في الفَقْرِ قد تناهى
وإنما وجبت له هذه الصفات، واستحال عليه أضدادها لأنه تعالى لو لم يكن موصوفا بها لكان بالسوى أي بسواها من الجهل والعجز وغيرهما ما تقدم من المستحيلات معروفا يعني موصوفا. أي أنه لو لم يكن متصفا بها لاتصف بأضدادها، لكن اتصافه تعالى بأضدادها باطل لما يلزم عليه من الافتقار والحدوث، كما أشار إليه بقوله: وكل من قام به سواها أي غيرها من الجهل أو ما في معناه أو العجز إلى آخر الأضداد، فهو الذي في الفقر أي الاحتياج إلى من يكمله، وهو متعلق بقوله: قد تناهى أي بلغ النهاية في الفقر، وهو محال لأنه يؤدي إلى الحدوث، فيكون من جملة العالم الحادث المفتقر.
44 - Because if He were not described * with them, He would be known by other than them. 45 - And whoever has in himself other than them * he is the one who has reached the ultimate in poverty. And indeed, these attributes are necessary for Him, and their opposites are impossible for Him, because the Exalted, if He were not described with them, He would be known by other than them, that is, by other than them from ignorance, incapacity, and other previously mentioned impossibles, meaning described. That is, if He were not characterized by them, He would be characterized by their opposites, but His being characterized by their opposites is invalid due to what follows from that of need and temporality, as He indicated by His saying: And whoever has in himself other than them, i.e., other than them from ignorance or what is in its meaning, or incapacity, up to the rest of the opposites, he is the one in poverty, i.e., need for one who completes him, and it is attached to His saying: has reached the ultimate, i.e., has reached the utmost limit in poverty, and that is impossible because it leads to temporality, so he would be part of the temporal, needy world.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the necessity of the attributes of meanings (ṣifāt al-maʿānī) for God. The author begins by stating that these attributes are necessary (wājiba) for God and their opposites are impossible (mustaḥīla). The reasoning is that if God were not described with these perfect attributes, He would necessarily be described with their opposites, such as ignorance and incapacity. However, being characterized by these opposites is invalid because they entail need (iftiqār) and temporality (ḥudūth), both of which are impossible for God. The author then cites verse 45 to illustrate: whoever has in himself something other than these attributes—meaning the opposites—has reached the ultimate level of poverty, which is need for a completer. This need leads to temporality, and thus such a being would belong to the contingent, temporal world. Therefore, the absence of the necessary attributes would imply the presence of their opposites, which leads to contingency—an impossibility for God. Hence, the attributes are necessary.

Key Terms
صفات المعاني
الافتقار
الحدوث
الأضداد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the proof assumes the attributes before proving them.
Correction: The proof actually proceeds from the impossibility of the opposite: if the opposite is impossible, then the attribute is necessary.

Checkpoint

B) Because they entail need and temporality
C) Because they are not mentioned in the Quran
D) Because they are possible

Key Takeaway
The necessity of God's attributes is proven by the impossibility of their opposites, which would entail need and temporality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

How will you let the necessity of all His attributes shape your worship and submission today?

The Worshipped One's Independence as Proof
Dardeer presents a syllogistic proof that the Worshipped One cannot need anything.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the statement 'the Worshipped One does not need others' functions as a syllogistic proof for the impossibility of God having opposites.

Core Idea
Worship implies independence; independence negates opposites.

This passage deepens the case against opposites in God by introducing a second proof built on the concept of worship. Dardeer shows that the very fact that God is worshipped entails that He cannot need anything, which in turn disproves any opposites that would imply neediness and contingency. The argument is condensed into a syllogism that we must reconstruct.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once without analysis. Let its rhythm sink in before you dissect the logic.
Notice the waw at the beginning – Dardeer glosses it.
2
Identify the syllogism components
The passage states a minor premise (every worshipped does not need others) and implies a major premise (whoever is utterly needy is temporal) leading to a conclusion. Find each part.
The major premise and conclusion are omitted but reconstructed.
3
Connect to the hypothetical syllogism
Understand how this categorical syllogism supports the 'istithna'iyya' proof – that God's being characterized by opposites is invalid.
4
Reflect on the theological climax
The passage ends by glorifying God as al-Ghani and al-Muqtadir. See how this seals the argument: His perfection negates any need or opposite.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والواو في قولنا: والواحد المعبود للحال، لا يفتقر لغيره، وهو في المعنى دليل لقولنا: وكل من قام به سواها ... إلخ لأنه في قوة قولنا: لأنه معبود، وكل معبود لا يفتقر لغيره، وقد حذفنا كبرى القياس مع النتيجة، والتقدير: وكل من تناهى في الفقر فهو حادث، فكل من قام به سواها فهو حادث كما أشرنا له في التقرير. وهذا القياس دليل الاستثنائية المطلوبة، أعني قولنا لكن اتصافه بأضدادها باطل، كما أشرنا له أيضًا. جل عن ذلك الافتقار الغني بالسكون للوزن، أي عن كل ما سواه، لاتصافه تعالى بكل كمال، وتنزهه عن كل نقص المقتدر على كل شيء، وكل شيء فهو إليه فقير.
And the waw in our saying: 'And the One, the Worshipped' is for the circumstance (of being in a state of not needing others), 'does not need others'—and it is in meaning a proof for our saying: 'And whoever has in himself other than them... etc.' because it is in the strength of our saying: 'Because He is worshipped, and every worshipped does not need others.' And we have omitted the major premise of the syllogism along with the conclusion, and the estimate (is): And whoever reaches the ultimate in poverty is temporal, so whoever has in himself other than them is temporal, as we indicated in the exposition. And this syllogism is a proof for the desired hypothetical syllogism (istithna'iyya), namely our saying: 'But His being characterized by their opposites is invalid,' as we have also indicated. He is exalted above that need, the Self-Sufficient (al-Ghani) with sukūn for the meter, i.e., above everything other than Him, because of His being characterized by every perfection and His being transcendent above every deficiency, the All-Powerful (al-Muqtadir) over everything, and everything is in need of Him.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage presents a second argument for the impossibility of God having the opposites of the necessary attributes, using a syllogistic proof. The author points to the verse 'And the One, the Worshipped, does not need others' as containing a proof. The argument is reconstructed: The minor premise is that every worshipped being does not need others. The major premise (omitted but implied) is that whoever reaches the ultimate in poverty (i.e., has the opposites) is needy and therefore temporal. The conclusion then is that whoever has the opposites is temporal. The complete syllogism is a hypothetical disjunctive (istithnā'iyya) that supports the earlier claim that God's being characterized by opposites is invalid. The passage ends by glorifying God as al-Ghanī (Self-Sufficient) and al-Muqtadir (All-Powerful), to whom all things are needy, reinforcing His independence from any deficiency.

Key Terms
الواحد المعبود
القياس
الاستثنائية
الغني
المقتدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument from worship is independent of the previous argument about opposites.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that this syllogism is a proof for the hypothetical syllogism ('But His being characterized by their opposites is invalid'), showing it is logically linked and reinforces the same conclusion.

Checkpoint
What is the role of the statement 'والواحد المعبود لا يفتقر لغيره' in the syllogism?
A) It is the major premise
B) It is the minor premise
C) It is the conclusion
D) It is a clarification of the attribute of power

Key Takeaway
The argument from worship establishes that the Worshipped One cannot need others, proving that He cannot have opposites which entail contingency and temporality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God is al-Ghani, completely self-sufficient, what does that mean for your motivation to worship? Is your prayer ever a transaction to get something from Him? How would it change if you truly believed He needs nothing from you?
?
When you face a problem, do you internally think God 'needs' your devotion to fix it? This lesson says God is beyond all need. How does that confront your assumption that your worship earns you favors?
?
Consider a sin you keep repeating. Does part of you think God is 'impoverished' without your obedience? The proof shows God is independent of your actions. Does that freedom liberate you to obey out of love rather than fear of loss?

God's Possible Acts and Temporal Attributes of Action
Dardeer defines what is possible for God and explains attributes of action as originated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Dardeer distinguishes God's possible actions from His essential attributes, and why attributes of action are considered temporal.

Core Idea
God's actions are possible and temporal, unlike His eternal essence.

In this passage, Dardeer completes his discussion of the necessary and impossible categories and turns to what is possible for God. He explains that creating or not creating, and granting happiness or misery, are all within God's power. But these acts are not eternal; they are temporal attachments of divine power, called attributes of action. This distinction is crucial for understanding God's transcendence and relationship with creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and translation
Read the Arabic verse (line 47) and its translation. Notice that it follows the discussion of necessary and impossible, introducing the category of possible for God.
The verse mentions four things: creating, leaving, making miserable, making happy.
2
Understand the definition of ijād
The commentary defines 'creation' (ijād) as the attachment of divine power to the existence of a possible thing. Note that it is synonymous with bringing into existence.
Different attachments receive different names based on their object (life, death, provision).
3
Identify the temporal nature of attachments
The passage explicitly states that these attachments are temporal (ḥāditha) because they are actualizations of power. They are called attributes of action (ṣifāt al-afʿāl) and are definitely originated.
This distinguishes them from God's eternal essential attributes.
4
Reflect on the theological significance
Consider why this distinction matters: it preserves God's eternity and transcendence while accounting for His acts in time.
This is a key principle in Sunni kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما أنهى الكلام على قسمي الواجب والمستحيل، شرع في بيان الجائز فقال:
٤٧ - وجائز في حقه الإيجادُ * والترْكُ والإشقاء والإسعادُ
وجائز في حقه تعالى الإيجاد أي إيجاد الممكنات، سواء وجدت بالفعل أو لم توجد. والإيجاد والخلق بمعنى واحد، وهو تعلق القدرة بوجود المقدور، فإن تعلقت تعالى بالحياة سمي إحياء، وبالموت سمي إماتة، وبالمرزوق سمي رزقا وترزيقا، وهذه حادثة كما ترى، لأنها عبارة عن التعلق. التعلقات هي المسماة بصفات الأفعال، وهي التنجيزي للقدرة، وهو حادث قطعا.
And when he finished the discourse on the two categories of the necessary and the impossible, he began to explain the possible, saying: 47 - And it is possible in His right to create * and to leave, and to make miserable and to make happy. And it is possible in His right, the Exalted, to create (al-ijād), i.e., bringing possible things into existence, whether they exist in actuality or do not exist. And bringing into existence and creating are synonymous, and it is: the attachment of power to the existence of the thing over which it has power. For if it is attached to life, it is called giving life; to death, it is called causing death; to the provision, it is called providing and giving provision. And these are temporal, as you see, because they are expressions of the attachment. The attachments are what are called attributes of action (ṣifāt al-afʿāl), and they are the actualizing attachment of power, and it is temporal definitively.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a classification of what is possible (jā'iz) for God, following the discussion of the necessary and impossible. The author introduces verse 47, stating that it is possible for God to create or not to create, to make happy or miserable. The commentary explains that 'creation' (ījād) is the attachment (taʿalluq) of divine power to the existence of a possible thing, and it is synonymous with bringing into existence. Different attachments are named according to their object: giving life, causing death, providing sustenance. These attachments are temporal (ḥāditha) because they are actualizations of power that occur in time. They are called attributes of action (ṣifāt al-afʿāl), and they are definitely originated (ḥādith qaṭʿan). This distinguishes God's essential attributes, which are eternal, from His acts, which are temporal and contingent upon His will.

Key Terms
الجائز
الإيجاد
صفات الأفعال
التنجيزي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's acts of creating, giving life, etc., are eternal attributes like His knowledge or power.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that these attachments are temporal (ḥāditha) and definitely originated (ḥādith qaṭʿan), distinguishing them from eternal essential attributes.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the status of 'صفات الأفعال' (attributes of action)?
A) Eternal
B) Temporal (حادثة)
C) Necessary
D) Impossible

Key Takeaway
God's attributes of action are temporal actualizations of His power, distinct from His eternal essential attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's actions are temporary, moment-by-moment attachments of His power, then your very existence hangs on His constant 'creating' anew. Do you live as though each breath is a fresh act of God, or have you become numb to His continual sustaining? How can you awaken to that reality today?
?
The attributes of action are distinct from God's essence. When you picture God, do you tend to merge His actions into His nature, losing sight of His utter transcendence? What specific thought pattern can you change to honor His essence as beyond all temporal acts?
?
You read that God has the 'possible' to create or not create, to give happiness or misery. This means your ultimate state depends on His free choice, not on any necessity. Does that truth humble you enough to plead for His mercy every single day? What will you do differently in your du'a tonight?

The Permissible for God: Definition and Examples
Definition of ja'iz with examples of divine actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what is meant by 'permissible' (ja'iz) for God, especially regarding creation, and how actual divine acts are temporal.

Core Idea
Divine acts like creation are permissible, not necessary, and they are temporal.

In this section, Sanusi defines the category of 'permissible' for God, focusing on creation. He explains that divine power attaches to possible things in a temporal way, and this attachment is called by different names depending on its object.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the poetic line listing four examples.
The poetic line is a mnemonic.
2
Identify the four examples
Find the four permissible acts mentioned: creation, leaving, making miserable, and making happy. Understand that these are actions God may or may not do.
The focus is on creation.
3
Understand the definition of creation
Creation is defined as the attachment of power to the existence of a possible. Note how this attachment gets specific names based on its object (life, death, provision).
4
Recognize the temporality
The attachments are called 'temporal' because they are actualizing attachments, which are definitely temporal. Ask yourself: why is this important for theology?
This sets up the objections in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما أنهى الكلامَ على قِسمَيِ الواجب والمستحيل، شرع في بيان الجائز فقال:
٤٧ - وجائز في حقه الإيجادُ * والترْكُ والإشقاءُ والإسعادُ
وجائز في حقه تعالى الإيجادُ أي: إيجادُ المُمْكِناتِ، سَواءٌ وُجِدتُ بالفِعْلِ أو لم توجَدْ. والإيجاد والخلق بمعنى واحد، وهو: تعلّق القُدرةِ بوجودِ المقدورِ، فَإِنْ تعلَّقتْ تعالى بالحياة سُمِّيَ إحياء، وبالموتِ سُمّي إماتة، وبالمرزوقِ سُمِّيَ رَزْقًا وترزيقًا، وهذه حادثة كما ترى، لأنها عبارةٌ عَنِ التعلَّقِ التنجيزي للقدرة، وهو حادث قطعًا.
فَإِنْ قُلتَ: قَدْ تَقَدَّمَ أَنَّ تَعَلَّقَ القُدْرَةِ واجبٌ، فَكَيْفَ يُحكَمُ عليهِ هُنا بالجواز؟ قُلْتُ: الواجبُ التَّعلُّقُ الصلوحي القديم، أما التنجيزيُّ فجائز، وكلُّ جائز حادث.
فإِنْ قُلتَ: الخلق والإيجادُ مِنْ صِفاته تعالى، وكيفَ يَتَّصِفُ تعالى بالحوادثِ؟ قُلْنَا: هذه أُمور اعتباريَّةٌ تَعْرِضُ للقُدرةِ لا وُجودَ لها في الأذهان، ولا تحقَّقَ لها في نفسها، ككَونِه قَبلَ العالَم ومعه وبعده، فلا يلزم قيام الحوادث به تعالى.
And when he finished the discussion on the two divisions of the necessary and the impossible, he began to explain the permissible, saying: 47 – And permissible in His right is creation, and leaving, and making miserable, and making happy. And permissible in His right, exalted, is creation, i.e., bringing into existence of possibles, whether they exist in actuality or do not exist. And creation and bringing into existence have one meaning, which is: the attachment of power to the existence of the thing over which power is exercised. So if it attaches, exalted, to life, it is called giving life; to death, it is called causing death; to the provision, it is called providing and provisioning; and these are temporal as you see, because they are an expression of the actualizing attachment of power, and it is definitely temporal. If you say: It has preceded that the attachment of power is necessary, so how is it judged here as permissible? I say: The necessary attachment is the pre-eternal potential attachment, but the actualizing attachment is permissible, and everything permissible is temporal. If you say: Creation and bringing into existence are among His attributes, exalted, and how can He, exalted, be described by temporal things? We say: These are relational matters that occur to power; they have no existence in minds, nor realization in themselves, like His being before the world, with it, and after it; so the subsistence of temporal things in Him, exalted, does not follow.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a definition and defense of the category of 'permissible' (جايز) for God, specifically regarding creation and its temporal aspects. The author begins by transitioning from the earlier discussion of necessary and impossible to the permissible. He quotes a poetic line that lists four examples of permissible actions: creation (إيجاد), leaving (ترك), making miserable (إشقاء), and making happy (إسعاد). He then defines creation as the attachment of divine power (تعلق القدرة) to the existence of a possible thing. This attachment, when actualized, is called by specific names depending on its object (e.g., giving life, causing death). The author emphasizes that these actualized attachments are temporal (حادثة) because they are expressions of the 'actualizing attachment' (التعلق التنجيزي), which is itself temporal. An objection is raised: earlier it was established that the attachment of power is necessary (واجب) – so how can it be called permissible here? The answer distinguishes between two types of attachment: the pre-eternal potential attachment (التعلق الصلوحي القديم) which is necessary, and the actualizing attachment (التعلق التنجيزي) which is permissible and temporal. A second objection asks how God can be described by temporal things (الحوادث) if creation is an attribute. The answer is that these attachments are merely relational matters (أمور اعتبارية) that occur to power; they have no independent existence. Analogous to the fact that God is described by being 'before the world, with it, and after it' – these are relational descriptions that do not imply change in God. Thus, no temporal attribute subsists in God's essence.

Key Terms
الجائز
الإيجاد
التعلق التنجيزي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the meaning of 'creation' (al-ijad)?
A) The eternal will of God
B) The attachment of power to the existence of a possible thing
C) Bringing something from nothing
D) The pre-eternal attribute

Key Takeaway
The permissible actions of God, such as creation, are temporal actualizations of His power, not eternal necessities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe that your existence is a temporal act of God's power, brought into being by His permission. If you truly internalized that every moment you exist is a fresh actualization of His power, how would your sense of self-reliance change? What would you do today to live in awareness of your constant dependence on Him?
?
The passage says God may create or leave (not create) as He wills. Are you at peace with the aspects of your life that He has chosen to create—your circumstances, your abilities, your trials—or do you secretly wish He had left them differently? What would it cost you to surrender that wish and embrace His permissible decree?
?
If death is not a natural end but a specific, temporal act of God's power attaching to your body, how does that reshape your view of your own mortality? Would you still fear death, or would you prepare to meet the One who gives and takes life at His chosen moment? What concrete step can you take today to face that moment with faith?

Answering Objections on Temporal Divine Acts
Two objections and their refutations regarding temporal divine acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how theologians defend the coherence of permissible temporal acts by distinguishing between necessary pre-eternal attachment and permissible actualizing attachment, and by describing them as relational matters.

Core Idea
God's temporal acts are merely relational attachments, not changes in His essence.

After defining the permissible, the author anticipates two objections. The first challenges the consistency of calling attachment permissible when it was earlier called necessary. The second objects to describing God by temporal things. Sanusi's answers provide key distinctions in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the objections and answers
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note the structure: two 'if you say' statements followed by responses.
These are standard dialectical steps in kalam.
2
Distinguish the two attachments
Identify the two types of attachment: pre-eternal potential (al-suluhi) which is necessary, and actualizing (al-tanjizi) which is permissible and temporal.
This resolves the first objection.
3
Understand 'relational matters'
The second objection is answered by stating that these temporal descriptions are merely relational (umur i'tibariyya) with no independent existence.
Analogous to saying God was 'before the world'.
4
Reflect on divine immutability
Consider how this explanation preserves God's essence from temporal change while allowing relational descriptions.
This is a key Ash'ari position.

The Permissibility of God's 'Leaving' (ترك)
Definition and examples of God's 'leaving' as a permissible act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that God's act of 'leaving' (ترك) possible things is purely permissible and not obligatory, and you will learn examples of this principle.

Core Idea
God's 'leaving' is just as permissible as His creating.

In this passage, Imam Dardīr explains another category of God's permissible acts: 'leaving' (الترك). This means that God may choose not to bring possible things into existence. The author emphasizes that this is not a defect but a matter of divine will, and he gives several examples to illustrate the principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of 'ترك'
Read the Arabic and translation for 'ترك' carefully. Note that it refers to leaving off creation of possible things.
The term 'ممكنات' refers to contingent beings that could exist or not.
2
Understand the principle of permissibility
The passage states that creation or leaving is equally permissible for God. Reflect on why this is important for understanding God's absolute freedom.
3
Examine the examples
Notice the examples given: sending messengers, vision of God, rewarding the disobedient, punishing the obedient. These are all possible acts that God may or may not do.
These examples show that God is not obligated to reward or punish in a particular way.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والترك) أَيْ: تَرَكُ الإيجادِ للمُمكناتِ، سواءٌ وُجدت أو لم توجد، يعني: أنَّ إيجاد كُلِّ مُمكن أو تركه أمر جائز في حقه تعالى، إنْ شَاءَ فَعَلَ وَإِنْ شَاءَ تَرَكَ، وَمِنْ ذلك بَعثةُ الرُّسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام، ورؤية الباري تعالى، وإثابة العاصي، وتعذيب المطيع.
والإشقاء وهو: خلقُ قُدرةِ الكُفر، أو خلقُ الكُفْرِ في العَبدِ - والعياذ بالله تعالى ويُسمّى الخِذْلانَ ،والإضلال، وقيَّدَه الأشعري بحالة الموتِ، وأطلقه الماتريدي.
And leaving means: leaving off the creation of possibles, whether they exist or do not exist; meaning: that the creation of every possible or its leaving is a permissible matter in His right, exalted. If He wills, He does, and if He wills, He leaves. And among that are the sending of messengers, peace be upon them, and the vision of the Creator, exalted, and rewarding the disobedient, and punishing the obedient. And making miserable is: creating the power of unbelief, or creating unbelief in the servant – and God forbid – and it is called abandonment and misguidance, and al-Ash'ari restricted it to the state of death, while al-Maturidi made it unrestricted.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of two more items from the permissible acts of God: 'leaving' (الترك) and 'making miserable' (الإشقاء). First, 'leaving' means that God may choose not to bring possible things into existence. Just as creation is permissible, so is its absence. The author gives examples: the sending of messengers, the vision of God in the afterlife, rewarding the disobedient, and punishing the obedient – all are permissible and not obligatory. Second, 'making miserable' (الإشقاء) is defined in two ways: either creating the power to disbelieve (according to Imam al-Haramayn) or creating unbelief itself in the servant (according to al-Ash'ari). This act is also called abandonment (خذلان) and misguidance (إضلال). The passage then notes a difference between al-Ash'ari and al-Maturidi: al-Ash'ari restricts judgment of a person's misery to the state of death (i.e., they are only considered miserable if they die upon unbelief), whereas al-Maturidi applies the judgment more broadly, considering the person miserable if they are in a state of unbelief during life.

Key Terms
الترك
ممكنات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that if God leaves something undone, it is because He cannot do it, or that He is unjust.
Correction: This passage shows that 'leaving' is a deliberate and permissible act; God is fully capable of creating but chooses not to. It is not injustice.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does 'ترك' mean?
A) Leaving off creation of possible things
B) Creating all possible things
C) Neither creating nor leaving
D) Forcing creation into existence

Key Takeaway
God's 'leaving' is a permissible act of divine will, not a sign of inability or injustice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Can you identify a time in your life when you felt God had 'left' something undone, and how does this lesson challenge your assumption that He should have acted differently? Will you now submit to His choice, whether He creates or leaves?
?
If God's leaving is just as permissible as His creating, what does that mean for your expectations when you pray for something? Are you willing to accept that God may 'leave' your request unfulfilled, and still trust that His leaving is the best possible act?
?
The passage mentions that God may punish the obedient and reward the disobedient as possibilities. How does this truth confront your sense of justice in this world? What must change in your heart to truly accept that God's will is always right, even when it defies your expectations?

Understanding God's 'Making Miserable' (إشقاء) and the Ash'ari-Maturidi Difference
Definition of 'إشقاء' and the Ash'ari-Maturidi difference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of God's 'making miserable' (الإشقاء) and the key difference between the Ash'ari and Maturidi schools regarding when a person is judged to be in a state of misery.

Core Idea
'Making miserable' is God's creation of unbelief, but its judgment differs between Ash'aris and Maturidis.

This passage delves into another permissible divine act: 'making miserable' (الإشقاء). The author defines it as creating either the power to disbelieve or unbelief itself. He then notes a significant difference between Imam al-Ash'ari and Imam al-Maturidi: al-Ash'ari restricts the judgment of misery to the moment of death, while al-Maturidi applies it more broadly.

The Permissibility of Leaving Creation (Tark)
Definition of tark as a permissible act of God and examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concept of 'tark' as a permissible act of God and why it is not obligatory for God to create all possible things.

Core Idea
God's leaving things uncreated is as permissible as creating them.

In this passage, Imam al-Dardir clarifies an important aspect of divine attribute: the permissibility of God to leave possible things uncreated. This concept guards against the mistaken notion that God must create everything He can. The text defines 'tark' and illustrates it with examples from theology such as sending messengers and rewarding sinners.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the key term 'tark' and how it is defined.
2
Understand the definition of tark
Identify the core claim: bringing into existence or leaving any possible thing is equally permissible for God. There is no obligation to create or not create.
The phrase 'in shā’a fa‘ala wa in shā’a taraka' encapsulates the freedom of divine will.
3
Reflect on the examples
Consider why these examples were chosen: sending messengers, seeing God, rewarding the disobedient, punishing the obedient. They highlight that even these profound matters are within God's discretion.
These examples may seem surprising, which underscores the lesson: nothing in creation is owed to us.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والتركُ) أَيْ: تَرَكُ الإيجادِ للمُمكناتِ، سواءٌ وُجدت أو لم توجد، يعني: أنَّ إيجاد كُلِّ مُمكن أو تركه أمر جائز في حقه تعالى، إنْ شَاءَ فَعَلَ وَإِنْ شَاءَ تَرَكَ، وَمِنْ ذلك بَعثةُ الرُّسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام، ورؤية الباري تعالى، وإثابة العاصي، وتعذيب المطيع.

If He wills, He does, and if He wills, He leaves. And among that are: sending messengers, seeing the Creator, rewarding the disobedient, and punishing the obedient.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'tark' (leaving/not creating) as a permissible act for God. It clarifies that God's creating or not creating any possible thing is entirely within His discretion. It gives examples of permissible acts: sending messengers, the vision of God (in the afterlife), rewarding sinners, and punishing obedient ones. These are all examples of things that God may do or not do; they are not obligatory.

Takwin: The Maturidi Solution to Divine Causation
Dardeer discusses the Maturidi doctrine of takwin and its difference from qudra.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi doctrine of takwin, its distinction from qudra, and why it resolves the problem of divine causation.

Core Idea
Takwin: the eternal attribute that actually brings things into existence, while qudra only enables.

This passage presents the Maturidi solution to a key theological puzzle: if God's power (qudra) is equally related to doing and leaving, how can He bring things into existence? The Maturidis answer by positing a distinct eternal attribute called takwin (origination). Dardeer contrasts this with the Ash'ari view, clarifying the nature of divine attributes of action and why takwin does not necessitate the pre-eternity of created things.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two theological positions
Read the beginning of the passage noting how Dardeer distinguishes Ash'ari and Maturidi views on the attributes of causing misery and happiness.
The Ash'ari consider these as created attributes of action; the Maturidi as eternal.
2
Understand the concept of takwin
Focus on the definition: takwin is one eternal attribute of meaning subsisting in God's Essence, through which existence occurs in accordance with will.
Takwin is not the same as power; it is a distinct attribute.
3
Distinguish takwin from qudra
Note that power gives the soundness of effect (ability to do or not do), while takwin brings about actual existence. This is why power alone cannot be the principle of existence.
This distinction solves the problem of power being neutral to both action and inaction.
4
Reflect on the implications about eternity and change
Understand why takwin is eternal (as an attribute of essence) but its objects are temporal. Also see the difference between eternal determinations (ishqā' and is'ād) and changing actual states (shaqāwa and sa'āda).
The pre-eternity of the attribute does not require pre-eternity of its objects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما عندَ إمامنا الأشعري فلأنهما الإماتة على الشقاوة أو السعادة، فهما مِنْ صفات الأفعال، وهي عنده حادثةٌ، لأنها عبارةٌ عن تعلقِ القُدرةِ بالمقدور ، كما مرَّ. وأما عندَ الماتريدي فلأنهما قديمان كالإحياء والإماتة والخلق والرزق وجميع ما تعبر عنه بصفاتِ الأفعالِ فقدْ جَزَمَ الماتريدية بقدمها، ومجموعُها عِندَ محققيهم: عبارة عَنْ صِفةٍ واحدةٍ تُسمّى بالتكوين قائمة بذاته تعالى لكونها صفة معنى، كالقدرة والإرادة، يتأتى بها وُجود الأشياء على وَفقِ الإرادة. والفَرقُ بينَها وبَينَ القُدرةِ: أَنَّ القُدرةَ عِندَهم بها صِحَةُ التأثير في الممكن، والتكوين به وُجود الأشياء. وحاصله: أنه لا يصح أنْ يكونَ مَبدأُ الوُجودِ القُدرةَ؛ لأَنَّ أَثَرَهَا صِحَةُ الفِعْل والتَّرْكِ مِنَ الفاعِلِ، فتكون نسبتها إلى الطرفين على السواء، فلا بُدَّ مِنْ صِفةٍ أخرى بها الصدور - وهي التكوين - فهي ليست التعلقَ التنجيزي للقُدرةِ حتى تكونَ حادثةٌ وجائزة، والجائز إنما هو الحدوث وعدمه، لا الإيجاد فإنه قديمٌ لكونه صفةً ذاته تعالى، فالإشقاء والإسعاد لا يتبدَّلان لقدَمِها؛ لما علمت أنهما يرجعان إلى التكوين، الذي هو صفةُ ذاته تعالى، والشقاوة والسعادة يتبدلان لأنهما الكُفرُ والإيمانُ، لا الموتِ على ذلك. ولا يلزَمُ مِنْ قِدَم التكوين قِدَمُ المَكَوَّنِ، إِذْ لا يلزمُ مِنْ قِدَم الصفة قِدَمُ متعلقها . وجُملةُ القَولِ في ذلك: أنَّ الإيجاد والخلق والرزق والإحياء والإماتة والإشفاء
According to our Imam al-Ash'ari, they (i.e., causing misery and causing happiness) are causing death upon misery or happiness, so they are attributes of actions (ṣifāt al-af'āl), and they are created according to him, because they are the relation of power to the thing empowered, as passed. As for al-Maturidi, they are eternal, like giving life, causing death, creation, provision, and all that is called attributes of actions; the Maturidis have affirmed their pre-eternity. Their sum according to their verified scholars is: one attribute called takwin (origination), subsisting in the Essence of the Exalted, because it is an attribute of meaning (ṣifat ma'nā), like power and will; through it, the existence of things occurs in accordance with the will. The difference between it and power is that power, according to them, gives the soundness of effect in the possible, while takwin gives the existence of things. The summary: it is not correct that power be the principle of existence, because its effect is the soundness of doing and leaving from the agent, so its relation to both sides is equal. Thus, another attribute is necessary for bringing forth—that is takwin. So it is not the actual relation (ta'alluq tanjīzī) of power, such that it would be created and contingent. The contingent is only existence and non-existence, not bringing into existence, for it is eternal because it is an attribute of the Essence of the Exalted. So causing misery and causing happiness do not change due to their pre-eternity, because you know they go back to takwin, which is an attribute of His Essence. As for misery and happiness, they change because they are disbelief and faith, not death upon that. And it does not follow from the pre-eternity of takwin the pre-eternity of the originated thing, since it does not necessarily follow from the pre-eternity of an attribute the pre-eternity of its object. The summary of the matter: that bringing into existence, creation, provision, giving life, causing death, and curing...
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage compares Ash'ari and Maturidi positions on the nature of causing misery and happiness. For Ash'ari, these are attributes of actions, created, and are the relation of power to what is empowered. For Maturidi, they are eternal attributes of action, summarized under one attribute called takwin (origination), which is an attribute of meaning (ṣifat ma'nā) subsisting in the Essence. The difference between takwin and qudra (power) is that power only gives the soundness of effect (both doing and leaving), while takwin brings about existence. Therefore, existence cannot originate from power alone; a distinct attribute, takwin, is needed. This explains why ishqā' and is'ād (eternal attributes) do not change, while shaqāwa and sa'āda (actual states) can change. The passage also clarifies that the pre-eternity of takwin does not imply the pre-eternity of what is originated. The author ends by listing several attributes of action unified under takwin.

Key Terms
صفات الأفعال
التكوين
صفة المعنى
التعلق التنجيزي
قِدم الصفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that qudra and takwin are the same attribute, or that takwin is a temporal relation of power.
Correction: The passage clarifies that qudra only enables (soundness of effect), while takwin is a distinct eternal attribute that brings about existence. Takwin is not the ta'alluq tanjīzī of power.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidis, what is the attribute through which existence occurs?
A) Power (al-qudra).
B) Will (al-irāda).
C) Origination (al-takwīn).
D) Relation (al-ta'alluq).

Key Takeaway
The Maturidis affirm takwin as an eternal attribute of meaning distinct from qudra, through which God brings things into existence, solving the problem of power's neutrality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your existence at every moment is directly brought about by an eternal attribute of God, not merely enabled? How does that change the way you view your own actions and your dependence on Him? Commit today to consciously acknowledge His direct creation in every breath you take.
?
If takwin is eternal and unchanging, yet the things it produces are temporal, what does that tell you about the constancy of God's will to create and sustain? Does your daily life reflect a reliance on that constant act of creation, or have you grown complacent, attributing events to secondary causes instead of His ongoing origination?
?
The difference between the Ash'ari and Maturidi views is not merely academic: how you view divine causation affects your trust in God's power. Are you living as if God merely enables you, leaving you to act independently, or as if He is directly bringing every moment and every action into existence? Examine your heart: where do you feel a sense of autonomy that should be replaced with reliance on His takwin?

The Ashʿari View: Attributes of Action Are Created
Imam Dardeer states the Ashʿari position that attributes of action are created.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ashʿari theologians consider attributes of action like causing misery and happiness to be created rather than eternal.

Core Idea
Attributes of action are relations of power, and relations are not eternal.

Imam Dardeer presents the Ashʿari position on a crucial point of divine attributes. While some theological schools hold all divine attributes to be eternal, the Ashʿaris distinguish between attributes of essence and attributes of action. The latter, they argue, are created because they consist in the attachment of God's power to its objects—a relation that comes into being when the object does.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic text and its translation carefully. Notice how Imam Dardeer concisely defines the Ashʿari stance.
The phrase 'as has passed' refers to an earlier discussion about the nature of power (qudra).
2
Identify the key terms
Locate the terms 'attributes of action' (ṣifāt al-afʿāl), 'created' (ḥāditha), and 'attachment' (taʿalluq). Understand how they connect.
These terms are central to the argument.
3
Understand the reasoning
Ask: Why does the fact that these attributes are expressions of power's attachment make them created? Think about what 'attachment' implies about temporality.
The attachment of power to a specific object arises when that object exists.
4
Connect to the broader theology
Reflect on why this distinction matters. How does it preserve God's transcendence while affirming His active involvement in creation?
This aligns with the Ashʿari commitment to avoiding temporal change in God's essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما عندَ إمامنا الأشعري فلأنهما الإماتة على الشقاوة أو السعادة، فهما مِنْ صفات الأفعال، وهي عنده حادثةٌ، لأنها عبارةٌ عن تعلقِ القُدرةِ بالمقدور ، كما مرَّ.
As for according to our Imam al-Ash'ari, they (i.e., causing misery and causing happiness) are the causing of death upon misery or happiness, so they are from the attributes of actions, and they are created in his view, because they are an expression of the attachment of power (qudra) to the object of power (maqdur), as has passed.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the Ash'ari position on the attributes of action (sifāt al-af'āl). The author, Imam Dardeer, states that according to Imam al-Ash'ari, attributes like causing misery (ishqā') and causing happiness (is'ād) are among the attributes of actions. He explains that these attributes are created (ḥāditha) because they consist in the relation (ta'alluq) of divine power (qudra) to the object of power (maqdur). Since relations are not eternal but arise with their terms, the attributes of action are temporally originated. The phrase 'as has passed' refers to an earlier discussion establishing that power is an eternal attribute, but its attachments (ta'alluqāt) are contingent.

Key Terms
صفات الأفعال
الحدوث
التعلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some hold that all divine attributes are equally eternal, denying any distinction between attributes of essence and action.
Correction: Ashʿaris argue that attributes of action are expressions of God's power in relation to creation, and since relations are not eternal, these attributes are created.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Ashʿari, why are attributes of action like causing misery considered created?
A) Because they are not real attributes of God.
B) Because they are expressions of the attachment of power to the object of power, which is contingent.
C) Because they occur in time and God is beyond time.
D) Because they involve change in God's essence.

Key Takeaway
Attributes of action are created because they consist in God's power attaching to temporal objects, which implies contingency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's power attaches to your actions only at the moment they occur, does that truth change how you perceive His involvement in your daily choices? Will you consciously remind yourself tomorrow that each of your deeds is directly sustained by His power at that instant?
?
The passage teaches that causing misery and happiness are not eternal but are created attachments of power. If your ultimate state is determined at death through such a temporal attachment, does that move you to plead for His mercy now, knowing it is not fixed? What specific prayer will you make today to seek His happiness over misery?
?
You believe in God's infinite power, but do you live as if His power only applies to major events while your small, habitual sins are somehow outside His direct control? The lesson insists that every attachment of His power is temporal and specific. Which seemingly 'small' sin are you assuming God's power does not touch, and what will you do today to acknowledge His power over that very moment?
