The Maturidi Doctrine of Takwin: An Eternal Attribute of Bringing into Existence
Imam Dardeer expounds the Maturidi view that all attributes of action reduce to the single eternal attribute of takwin, distinguishing it from power and defending its eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi concept of takwin as a distinct eternal attribute of Allah, its relationship to power, and why it is necessary for explaining creation.

Core Idea
Takwin is the eternal attribute by which Allah brings things into existence, distinct from power which only enables.

Imam Dardeer now presents the Maturidi theological perspective on the 'attributes of action' (sifat al-af'al). The Maturidis affirm that these are eternal, rooted in a single attribute called takwin. This attribute is not merely a mode of power but a distinct quality that accounts for the actual coming-into-being of things. Before we dive into the Arabic, consider the problem: if God's power is equally able to create or not create, what specifies creation? The Maturidi answer is takwin.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without stopping. Let the flow of the author's logic come through. Then read the English translation.
2
Identify the key claims
What does the passage assert about the attributes of action? How does it define takwin? Why is it different from power?
Focus on the distinction between sihhat al-ta'thir and actual existence.
3
Understand the proof
Trace the argument that power cannot be the source of existence because it is neutral. Then see why takwin is needed.
Notice the phrase 'it is not valid for power to be the principle of existence'.
4
Address the objection
The passage ends by clarifying that the eternity of takwin does not imply the eternity of created things. Reflect on why this is important.
This prevents a possible misunderstanding about the co-eternity of the world.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما عندَ الماتريدي فلأنهما قديمان كالإحياء والإماتة والخلق والرزق وجميع ما تعبر عنه بصفاتِ الأفعالِ فقدْ جَزَمَ الماتريدية بقدمها، ومجموعُها عِندَ محققيهم: عبارة عَنْ صِفةٍ واحدةٍ تُسمّى بالتكوين قائمة بذاته تعالى لكونها صفة معنى، كالقدرة والإرادة، يتأتى بها وُجود الأشياء على وَفقِ الإرادة. والفَرقُ بينَها وبَينَ القُدرةِ: أَنَّ القُدرةَ عِندَهم بها صِحَةُ التأثير في الممكن، والتكوين به وُجود الأشياء. وحاصله: أنه لا يصح أنْ يكونَ مَبدأُ الوُجودِ القُدرةَ؛ لأَنَّ أَثَرَهَا صِحَةُ الفِعْل والتَّرْكِ مِنَ الفاعِلِ، فتكون نسبتها إلى الطرفين على السواء، فلا بُدَّ مِنْ صِفةٍ أخرى بها الصدور - وهي التكوين - فهي ليست التعلقَ التنجيزي للقُدرةِ حتى تكونَ حادثةٌ وجائزة، والجائز إنما هو الحدوث وعدمه، لا الإيجاد فإنه قديمٌ لكونه صفةً ذاته تعالى، فالإشقاء والإسعاد لا يتبدَّلان لقدَمِها؛ لما علمت أنهما يرجعان إلى التكوين، الذي هو صفةُ ذاته تعالى، والشقاوة والسعادة يتبدلان لأنهما الكُفرُ والإيمانُ، لا الموتِ على ذلك. ولا يلزَمُ مِنْ قِدَم التكوين قِدَمُ المَكَوَّنِ، إِذْ لا يلزمُ مِنْ قِدَم الصفة قِدَمُ متعلقها .
And as for according to al-Maturidi, they (i.e., causing misery and causing happiness) are eternal like giving life, causing death, creating, providing, and all that is expressed by attributes of actions; indeed the Maturidis decisively affirm their eternity. And their totality according to their verifiers is an expression of a single attribute called takwin (bringing into existence), subsisting in His essence, exalted, because it is an attribute of meaning (sifat ma'na), like power and will, by which the existence of things comes about in accordance with will. And the difference between it and power is that power, in their view, is the soundness of effect (sihhat al-ta'thir) upon the possible, while taking is the existence of things. The upshot is that it is not valid for power to be the principle of existence, because its effect is the soundness of doing and refraining on the part of the agent, so its relation to both sides is equal; therefore another attribute is necessary for emanation, and that is takwin. Thus it is not the actualized attachment (al-ta'allaq al-tanjizi) of power so that it would be created and contingent; the contingent is only arising or not arising, not bringing into existence (al-ijad), for it is eternal because it is an attribute of His essence, exalted. So causing misery and causing happiness do not change due to their eternity, because you have learned that they trace back to takwin, which is an attribute of His essence, exalted. And misery and happiness (shiqawa and sa'ada) change because they are disbelief and faith, not dying upon that. And it does not follow from the eternity of takwin the eternity of the thing brought into existence (al-mukawwan), since it does not follow from the eternity of the attribute the eternity of its object.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a definition and argumentative exposition of the Maturidi view on the attributes of action. The author begins by stating the Maturidi position: attributes like causing misery and happiness are eternal (qadim), as are all attributes of action such as giving life, causing death, creating, and providing. The Maturidis collectively affirm their eternity. He then explains that, according to their most rigorous verifiers (muhaqqiqun), all such expressions refer to a single attribute called takwin (bringing into existence). This attribute subsists in God's essence as an attribute of meaning (sifat ma'na), like power and will. Through takwin, things come into existence in accordance with divine will. The author then clarifies the difference between takwin and power: power is the ability (sihhat al-ta'thir) to act or refrain, while takwin is the actual bringing into existence. He proves why power cannot be the principle of existence: power's effect is balanced between doing and not doing, so an additional attribute is needed to specify existence. This attribute is takwin, which is not a contingent attachment of power but an eternal attribute. Thus, causing misery and happiness are eternal because they belong to takwin, an essential attribute, while the states of misery and happiness (belief and disbelief) themselves change. He also addresses a potential objection: the eternity of takwin does not imply the eternity of the things it brings into existence, as there is no necessary correlation between the eternity of an attribute and the eternity of its object.

صفات الأفعال
التكوين
القدرة
الإرادة
صِحَةُ التأثير
التعلق التنجيزي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that takwin is a temporal act of creation or identical to power.
Correction: Takwin is a co-eternal attribute distinct from power, responsible for bringing existence about, and its eternity does not make created things eternal.

Checkpoint
Why do Maturidis distinguish takwin from power?
A) Because power is an essential attribute while takwin is a contingent one.
B) Because power enables both acting and refraining, while takwin specifically brings things into existence.
C) Because takwin is the same as power but with a different name.
D) Because power is created and takwin is eternal.

Key Takeaway
Takwin is the eternal divine attribute of bringing into existence, distinct from power and will, and its eternity does not imply the eternity of created beings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every action of yours is brought into existence by Allah's eternal attribute of takwin, and you have the power (qudra) to act or refrain, how does your responsibility for your deeds remain? Are you truly the author of your actions, or do you merely choose while Allah creates? Examine your sense of accountability in light of this teaching. What change in your attitude toward sin does this demand?
?
The passage distinguishes between the ability to act (qudra) and the actual existence of the act (takwin). When you struggle with a sin, do you truly rely on Allah to bring about your obedience through His takwin, or do you lean on your own ability? Consider your next moment of temptation: will you remember that your ability alone is insufficient and that only Allah's bringing into existence can make you obey? What will you do differently?
?
Takwin is eternal, but its objects—your faith, your deeds, your very being—are contingent and subject to change. Your current state of belief is not guaranteed to last. Does this truth comfort you or unsettle you? How will you seek to have your faith continually brought into existence by Allah's attribute of takwin? What is one specific supplication (du'a) you will make today to ask Allah to preserve your faith?

Ash'ari and Maturidi on Created Attributes: The Refined View
Imam Dardeer summarizes both schools and presents the refined Ash'ari position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference between the Ash'ari and Maturidi views on attributes like creation and the refined Ash'ari position that power and will suffice without an eternal attribute of takwin.

Core Idea
The refined Ash'ari view eliminates the need for an eternal attribute of 'making'—power and will are enough.

Imam Dardeer presents a doctrinal summary that contrasts the Ash'ari and Maturidi schools on the nature of divine attributes related to creation. He then clarifies the refined Ash'ari position held by the verifying scholars, which simplifies the divine attributes to power and will alone. This passage is a key example of how kalam theology balances philosophical rigor with scriptural fidelity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two schools' positions
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting the difference between Ash'ari (صفات حادثة) and Maturidi (صفة أزلية) views.
The Maturidis call the eternal attribute 'takwin'.
2
Understand the concept of takwin
The Maturidis argue that attributes like creating are manifestations of a single eternal attribute called takwin, which is the source of emanation.
Takwin is additional to power and will.
3
Grasp the refined Ash'ari argument
The verifiers among Ash'aris hold that no additional attribute is needed: power with will is enough to specify and bring about existence.
This simplifies the divine attributes to power and will alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجُملةُ القَولِ في ذلك: أنَّ الإيجاد والخلق والرزق والإحياء والإماتة والإشفاء والإسعادَ والتصوير، إلى غير ذلك عند الأشعرية صفات حادثة، لأنها إضافات و اعتبارات بينَ القدرة والمقدور، وعِندَ الماتريدية قديمة لأنها صفة أزلية بها صدور العالم وكل جزء مِنْ أجزائه، وتُسمّى تكوينا، لكنْ إِنْ تَعلَّقتْ بِوُجودِ الشَّيءِ سُمّيت إيجاداً وخلقا، أو بمَوتِه سُمّيت إماتة، أو بصورته سُمّيت تصويرا، وهي زائدة على القُدرة والإرادة، فالإرادة بها التخصيص، والقُدرة هي القوة على فعل الشيء أو تركه، ونسبة الأمرين إليها على السواء، فليس بها صُدور الأشياء، وإنما بها قبول مبْدأُ لقبول الصُّدور، والتكوينُ مبداً لنفس الصُّدور. و المُحقِّقُونَ مِنَ الأَشاعِرِةِ على أَنه لَيسَ فِي الأَزَلِ إلا مبدأ الإيجاد والإشقاء والإسعاد وغير ذلك، ولا دليل على صفةٍ أخرى سوى القُدرةِ والإرادةِ، فَإِنَّ القُدرةَ وإِنْ كانَ نسبها إلى وُجودِ المُكوَّنِ وعَدَمِه على السواء، لكِنْ مَعَ انْضِمام الإرادةِ يتخَصَّصُ أَحَدُ الجانبين. وإنَّما نصَّ على الإشقاءِ والإسعادِ وإِنْ دخَلا في الإيجادِ اهتماما بشأنهما.
The summary of the statement regarding that is: bringing into existence, creating, providing, giving life, causing death, curing, causing happiness, and forming, and so on, are according to the Ash'aris created attributes, because they are additions (idafat) and considerations (i'tibarat) between power and the object of power; and according to the Maturidis they are eternal because they are an eternal attribute by which the world and every part of its parts emanates, and it is called takwin; but if it is attached to the existence of a thing it is called bringing into existence and creating, or to its death it is called causing death, or to its form it is called forming; and it is additional to power and will, for by will is specification (takhsis), and power is the capacity to do or refrain from a thing, and the relation of both actions to it is equal, so by it (power) there is no emanation of things, but rather by it there is acceptance, a principle for acceptance of emanation, and takwin is a principle for the emanation itself. And the verifiers (muhaqqiqun) among the Ash'aris are of the opinion that there is not in pre-eternity any principle of bringing into existence, causing misery, causing happiness, and so on except power and will, and there is no evidence for another attribute besides power and will, for power even if its relation to the existence of the thing brought into existence and its non-existence is equal, yet with the joining of will one of the two sides becomes specified. And he (the author) mentioned 'causing misery' and 'causing happiness' specifically, even though they are included in 'bringing into existence', out of concern for their importance.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a comparative summary and a doctrinal refinement. The author, Imam Dardeer, first recapitulates the two positions: Ash'aris consider attributes like creating, providing, etc., as created (haditha) because they are merely relations (idafat) and considerations (i'tibarat) between divine power and its objects. Maturidis, on the other hand, deem them eternal because they constitute a single eternal attribute called takwin, which is the source of emanation for every part of creation. This attribute is additional to power and will: will specifies which possibility to actualize, power enables acting or refraining, and takwin brings about existence. The author then presents the refined Ash'ari position (muhaqqiqun min al-Ash'ira): there is no need to posit an additional attribute like takwin in eternity; only power and will suffice. Although power's relation to existence and non-existence is equal, the addition of will tilts the scale, specifying one side. The mention of causing misery and happiness, though these are aspects of bringing into existence, is given special emphasis due to their theological significance.

Key Terms
صفات الأفعال
الإضافات والاعتبارات
التكوين
التحقيق
التخصيص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ash'ari refined position denies that God creates or that creation is real.
Correction: No, it affirms that God creates through power and will; it just denies an additional eternal attribute of 'making'.

Checkpoint
According to the refined Ash'ari position (muhaqqiqun), why is there no need for an attribute like takwin in addition to power and will?
A) Because takwin is identical to power.
B) Because power and will together are sufficient to specify and bring about existence.
C) Because Maturidis do not actually believe in takwin.
D) Because existence is not an action of God.

Key Takeaway
The refined Ash'ari position holds that only power and will are necessary divine attributes for creation; will specifies what power does.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience a trial, do you truly believe that God's power and will alone brought it about with precise specification, or do you credit secondary causes as if they act independently? How should this understanding change your reaction to hardship?
?
The passage highlights that causing misery and happiness are included in bringing into existence. If every event—your joys and sorrows—is directly from God's power and will alone, how does this shape the way you receive both? What would it mean to thank Him equally for each?
?
Knowing that will specifies every detail of your existence, is there an area of your life where you resist God's specification, desiring your own choice instead? What would it take to submit fully to His will as the sole determinant of your state?

Ash'ari and Maturidi Views on Takwin
Dardeer compares Ash'ari and Maturidi views on takwin and related attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key difference between Ash'ari and Maturidi schools regarding the attribute of takwin (bringing into existence) and why Ash'aris consider creative attributes as temporal relations.

Core Idea
For Ash'aris, creative attributes are mere relations; for Maturidis, they are aspects of one eternal attribute, takwin.

This passage from Imam Dardeer's commentary on al-Kharidah explores a foundational theological disagreement between the Ash'ari and Maturidi schools. It focuses on the nature of divine attributes related to creation, such as granting happiness and forming. Understanding this difference is crucial for grasping later debates on divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with footnotes
Read the Arabic passage once, including the footnotes. Then read the translation. Notice that the footnotes provide important clarifications on the nature of the attributes and the meaning of 'sudur'.
The footnotes are part of the original text.
2
Identify the Ash'ari position on temporal attributes
Locate where the text states that for Ash'aris, attributes like is'ad and taswir are 'haditha' (temporal) because they are 'idafat wa i'tibar' (relations and considerations).
This is the first major claim.
3
Identify the Maturidi position on eternal takwin
Find where the Maturidi view is presented: they consider all these as aspects of one eternal attribute called takwin, which is the principle of the world's emergence.
Takwin is additional to power and will.
4
Understand the objection and its answer
Read footnote (1) that answers how God can be described by temporal attributes. The answer is that they are mere relations, not real existent entities.
This addresses a potential theological issue.
5
Examine the roles of power, will, and takwin
Note the explanation: power is neutral, will specifies, and takwin is the principle of actual coming into existence. The verifiers' final position clarifies that only power and will are needed.
This refines the Ash'ari stance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الأول: الإلهيات
والإسعادَ والتصوير، إلى غير ذلك عند الأشعرية صفات حادثة، لأنها إضافات و اعتبارات ( بَينَ القدرة والمقدور، وعِندَ الماتريدية قديمة لأنها صفة أزلية بها صدور العالم وكل جزء مِنْ أجزائه، وتُسمّى تكوينا، لكنْ إِنْ تَعلَّقتْ بِوُجودِ الشَّيءِ سُمّيت إيجاداً وخلقا، أو بمَوتِه سُمّيتْ إماتة، أو بصورته سُمّيت تصويرا، وهي زائدة على القذرة والإرادة، فالإرادة بها التخصيص، والقُدرة هي القوة على فعل الشيء أو تركه، ونسبة الأمرين إليها على السواء، فليس بها صُدور الأشياء، وإنما بها قبول مبْدأُ لقبول الصُّدور، والتكوينُ مبداً لنفس الصُّدور. الصُّدور (٢)، فهي
(۱) هذا جواب عن كيف يتصف الله بها وهي حادثة ؟ فالجواب أنها إضافات و اعتبارات، وليست أمورًا وجودية.
(۲) الصدور أي بروز العالم ووجوده بعد عدمه.
والمُحقِّقُونَ مِنَ الأَشاعِرِةِ على أَنه لَيسَ فِي الأَزَلِ إلا مبدأ الإيجاد والإشقاء والإسعاد وغير ذلك، ولا دليل على صفةٍ أخرى سوى القُدرةِ والإرادةِ، فَإِنَّ القُدرةَ وإِنْ كانَ نسبها إلى وُجودِ المُكوَّنِ وعَدَمِه على السواء، لكِنْ مَعَ انْضِمام الإرادةِ يتخَصَّصُ أَحَدُ الجانبين. وإنَّما نصَّ على الإشقاءِ والإسعادِ وإِنْ دخَلا في الإيجادِ اهتماما بشأنهما.
The first section: Divine matters. And granting happiness and forming [creation], and so on, according to the Ash'aris are temporal attributes, because they are relations and considerations between power and the empowered. According to the Maturidis they are eternal because they are an eternal attribute by which the world and every part of its parts come into existence, and it is called takwin (bringing into existence). But if it is related to the existence of a thing it is called ijad (creating) and khalq (creation), or to its death it is called imata (causing death), or to its form it is called taswir (forming). And it is additional to power and will. For will is for specification, and power is the capacity to do or leave a thing, and the relation of both [existence and non-existence] to it is equal. So by it [power] things do not come into existence, rather by it there is acceptance, a principle for the acceptance of coming into existence, and takwin is a principle for the very coming into existence. (1) This is an answer to how God is described by these [attributes] while they are temporal? The answer is that they are relations and considerations, not existent things. (2) Al-sudur means the emergence of the world and its existence after its non-existence. And the verifiers among the Ash'aris hold that in eternity there is only the principle of bringing into existence, causing misery, granting happiness, and other [acts], and there is no evidence for another attribute besides power and will. For power, even if its relation to the existence and non-existence of the thing is equal, yet with the addition of will one of the two sides becomes specified. He specifically mentioned causing misery and granting happiness even though they are included in bringing into existence out of concern for their importance.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage defines the first section (Ilahiyyat) and discusses the divine attributes related to creative acts. It begins by stating that according to the Ash'aris, attributes such as granting happiness (is'ad) and giving form (taswir) are temporal (haditha) because they are relational (idafat) and conceptual (i'tibar), not real existent attributes. The Maturidis, however, consider them eternal (qadima) as aspects of a single eternal attribute called takwin (bringing into existence), which is the principle of the world's emergence. This attribute, when related to existence is called ijad, to death imata, to form taswir, etc. It is additional to power (qudra) and will (irada). Will specifies, power is equal in ability to do or not do. Then the author provides a footnote addressing how God can be described by temporal attributes, answering that they are mere relations, not real existent entities. A second footnote defines sudur as the world's emergence after non-existence. The passage then turns to the 'verifiers among the Ash'aris' who hold that in eternity there is only the principle of bringing into existence, causing misery, and granting happiness, and no separate attribute besides power and will. They argue that power alone is neutral, but when combined with will, one of the two possibilities is specified. The mention of causing misery and granting happiness is emphasized because of their great significance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that all attributes of God are equally eternal and real.
Correction: This passage shows that Ash'aris consider some attributes (like forming and granting happiness) as temporal because they are merely relations and considerations, not real eternal attributes.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'aris, why are attributes like taswir (forming) considered temporal?
A) Because they are not mentioned in the Qur'an.
B) Because they are relations and considerations (idafat wa i'tibar), not real attributes.
C) Because God does not actually perform these acts.
D) Because they are created in time.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari and Maturidi schools differ fundamentally on whether creative attributes are eternal or temporal, but both affirm God's power and will in creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own existence—your life, death, and form—do you sense that Allah's creative act (takwin) is a direct and eternal involvement, or do you tend to see it as merely the result of a neutral power and will? How does that shape your daily reliance on Him?
?
The passage emphasizes that causing misery and granting happiness are singled out for importance. When you face a trial or a blessing, do you consciously connect it to Allah's attribute of takwin, or do you attribute it to secondary causes? What would change if you saw every moment as a direct expression of His eternal creative act?
?
The Ash'aris warn against unnecessarily multiplying attributes without evidence. Are there aspects of your belief about Allah that you hold without clear textual warrant? Are you willing to let go of comforting ideas about God that are not grounded in revelation and sound reasoning, even if they feel reassuring?

The Beatific Vision: Seeing Allah in Paradise
Dardeer explains the necessity and nature of the beatific vision in Paradise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic belief in the beatific vision (ru'ya) in Paradise as a real sight without spatial constraints, its universality for all believers, and its variation based on one's knowledge and love of Allah.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah in Paradise is real, without place or direction, and varies in degree.

In this passage, Imam Dardeer clarifies a core Sunni belief: that believers will see Allah in Paradise. He explains what this seeing entails—it is a complete unveiling by sight, yet without the limitations of physical vision like location, distance, or direction. He also affirms that every inhabitant of Paradise, including women and children, will experience this vision, though its intensity differs according to one's knowledge and love of Allah in this world.

Guided Path
1
Understand the obligatory nature
Notice how Dardeer begins with a command ('be certain') and emphasizes that belief in the vision is obligatory for every Muslim.
This counters those who reject or metaphorize the vision.
2
Grasp the modality of the vision
Focus on the description: the vision is without limit, place, direction, distance, or ray. It is a complete unveiling by sight, but not like physical sight.
The Ash'ari position is that vision occurs by Allah's creation in the seer, not through normal conditions.
3
Recognize the universality
See that all inhabitants of Paradise, including jinn, women, and children, will see Allah. The vision is not exclusive to prophets or saints.
4
Reflect on differentiation
Understand that the vision varies in quality, quantity, and pleasure according to one's knowledge and love of Allah in this world.
This motivates increasing faith in worldly life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واجزم أخي برؤية الإله * في جنة الخلد بلا تناهي (واجزم) أي: اقطع واعتقد وُجوبًا (أخي) في الإسلام، إذ الأب الذي خرجنا صلى الله (۱) رؤية بسبه مِنْ ظُلمةِ الكُفْرِ إلى نور الإيمانِ واحِدٌ، وهو النبي )، (برؤية الإله) سبحانه وتعالى، بمعنى الانكشاف التام بالبصر ")، أي: بوقوعها (في جنّةِ الخُلْدِ) أي: الإقامة على سبيل الدوام حال كون الرؤية حاصلة (بلا) تناهي) للمرئي تعالى، أي: مِنْ غَير إحاطة بحدودِ المرئي ونهاياته، لاستحالة الحدودِ والنهايات عليه تعالى. فكما أنهم يعلَمونَه بلا حَدٌ ونهاية وبلا كيف، يَرَونَه كذلك، فيُرى لا في مكان ولا في جهةٍ، ولا باتِّصالِ شُعاع، ولا على مسافةٍ بَينَه تعالى وبَينَ الرائي، لأنَّ الرؤيةً عِندَنا(۳) بخلْقِ اللَّهِ تعالى في أَيِّ مَحَلٌّ شَاءَ، وليس بلازم ألا يكون إلا عِندَ اجتماع الشرائط) كما سيأتي توضيحه. وتقعُ لكل مَنْ دخَلَ الْجَنَّةَ، مِنْ إِنسِ وجِنَّ مِنْ هذه الأمّةِ وغَيرها، حتى النِّساءِ و الصبيان (٦) . وتتفاضَلُ الرؤية كما وكيفا ولذَّةَ على قدْرِ العِلْم باللهِ وحُبِّه في الدنيا، حتى إِنَّ البعض ذكروا . (١) لا تنقطع عنه أبدا، كما أنه كانَ في الدُّنيا لا يتعلَّقُ قلبه بِغَيرِ اللَّهِ تعالى أبدا، كذا
And be certain, my brother, of seeing the God * in the garden of eternity without finitude. (And be certain) i.e. decisively believe and hold as obligatory (my brother) in Islam, since the father who brought us out صلى الله (۱) from the darkness of disbelief to the light of faith is one, and he is the Prophet ), (of seeing the God) glorified and exalted, meaning the complete unveiling by sight "), i.e. its occurrence (in the garden of eternity) i.e. residence on the way of perpetuity while the vision is occurring (without) finitude) of the seen, exalted, i.e. without encompassing the limits of the seen and its ends, due to the impossibility of limits and ends upon Him, exalted. So just as they know Him without limit, end, and without how, they see Him likewise, so He is seen not in a place nor in a direction, nor with the connection of a ray, nor at a distance between Him, exalted, and the seer, because the vision according to us (3) is by the creation of Allah, exalted, in whatever place He wills, and it is not necessary that it be only when the conditions are met) as will be clarified later. And it occurs for everyone who enters Paradise, from humans and jinn from this community and others, even women and children (6). And the vision differs in quantity, quality, and pleasure according to the extent of knowledge of Allah and love of Him in this world, such that some have mentioned (1) that it never ceases from him, just as in this world his heart was never attached to other than Allah, exalted, forever, likewise.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the verse commanding belief in the beatific vision. It first defines the key terms: 'be certain' means to have decisive obligatory belief, and 'my brother' refers to a fellow Muslim, since the Prophet (PBUH) is the spiritual father who brought believers from darkness to light. 'Seeing the God' means complete unveiling by sight, occurring in the eternal Garden, without finitude of the seen (i.e., without encompassing limits, which are impossible for Allah). Then it clarifies the modality: just as believers know Allah without limit, end, or 'how', they see Him likewise—not in a place, direction, with a ray, or at a distance. This is because the vision, according to the Ash'aris, is created by Allah in whichever place He wills, and it is not necessary that conditions of normal sight (like distance and direction) hold; they are merely customary, not rational. The vision occurs for all who enter Paradise, including humans, jinn, women, and children. Furthermore, the vision differs in quantity, quality, and pleasure according to one's knowledge and love of Allah in the world. Some have said that the vision of the beloved (those who were entirely devoted to Allah) never ceases, just as their hearts were never attached to other than Allah in this world.

Imagine that you are shown a preview of your future vision of Allah—the degree of unveiling you will receive. If it is less than you hoped, what specific change will you make this week to increase your knowledge and love of Him?

The Scriptural Proof for Ru'ya from Moses' Request
Presents a sam'iyy proof for the possibility of ru'ya based on Moses' request and answers an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural proof for the possibility of seeing Allah based on Moses' request, and how the Ash'ari response refutes the Mu'tazili objection.

Core Idea
Moses' request proves ru'ya is possible because prophets never ask for the impossible.

This lesson examines a key scriptural (sam'iyy) proof for the permissibility of seeing Allah: the request of Prophet Moses as recorded in the Qur'an. It shows why the request itself implies that ru'ya is possible, and then addresses a major objection often raised by those who deny it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. This will give you the full argument in the author's own words.
Notice how the passage is structured: a proof statement, then an objection, then a response.
2
Understand the core proof
The proof has two parts: (1) Moses, as a prophet, would not ask for something impossible, so ru'ya must be possible. (2) Allah conditioned ru'ya on the possible event of the mountain settling, and a condition on a possible makes the conditioned possible.
3
Examine the objection and answer
The Mu'tazila object that Moses asked to teach his people that ru'ya is impossible, and that the condition (settling while moving) is impossible. The answer shows these interpretations are forced and irrational.
Pay attention to how the answer refutes both parts of the objection without introducing new evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد استُدلَّ على الجواز أيضًا بدليل سمْعيّ (١)، وهو: أنَّ موسى عليه السلام قد سألها بقوله تعالى: ﴿رَبِّ أرني أنظُرْ إِلَيْكَ﴾ فلو لم تكن جائزة ما سألها، وإلا كانَ طلبها إمّا جهلًا بأحكام الألوهية، وإمّا سفَها أو عبَثًا بطَلَب المحال، والأنبياءُ مُنزَّهونَ عَنْ ذلك كُلَّه (۳)، وأنَّ الله تعالى قد علقها على مُمكن - وهو استقرار الجبل (٤) - والمعلَّق على المُمْكِن مُمكن، إذ معنى التعليق : الإخبارُ بوقوع المعلَّق عند ثبوتِ المُعلَّقِ عليه، والمحالُ لا يَقَعُ على شَيْءٍ مِنَ التقادير الممكنة)، فلو لَمْ تَكُنْ ممكنةً لزِمَ الخُلفُ (1) في خَبَره تعالى، وهو مُحالٌ. وما قيلَ مِنْ أَنَّ سؤال موسى عليه السلام لَم يَكُنْ لتحصيل مطلوبه، وإنما كان لتعليم قومه أنها ممتنعة حين قالوا له: ﴿لَن نُّؤْمِنَ لَكَ حَتَّى نَرَى الله﴾ (٩)، ولا نُسَلِّمُ أنَّ المُعلَّقَ عليه مُمكِنٌ، بل هو استقرار الجبل حالَ تحرُّكه (١٠) وهو مُحالٌ !؟ تجوابه أَنَّ كُلَّا مِنْ ذلك خِلافُ الظَّاهِرِ ، فلا وجْهَ للحَمْل عليه ، على أَنَّ قَومَه إن كانوا مؤمنين كفاهم قوله «إنها ممتنعة» وإلا لم يُصَدِّقوه في حُكْم الله بالامتناع، فالسؤال عبث على كل حال والاستقرار حالَ التَّحَرُّك مُمكن بأنْ يَقَعَ السُّكونُ بدَلَ الحركة، إنما المحالُ اجتِماعُ الحَرَكَةِ والسُّكونِ(۳).
It has also been argued for permissibility by a scriptural proof (sam'iyy): that Moses, peace be upon him, asked for it [i.e., seeing Allah] by His saying exalted: 'My Lord, show me [Yourself] that I may look upon You.' For if it were not permissible, he would not have asked for it; otherwise, his request would be either ignorance of the rulings of divinity, or foolishness or frivolity in seeking the impossible, and the prophets are free of all of that. And that Allah exalted conditioned it upon something possible – namely, the settling of the mountain – and that which is conditioned upon the possible is possible, since the meaning of conditioning is informing of the occurrence of the conditioned thing upon the establishment of the condition, and the impossible does not occur under any possible circumstances. So if it were not possible, then falsehood in His exalted information would follow, and that is impossible. And it has been said that Moses' question was not to obtain what he sought, but rather to teach his people that it is impossible when they said to him: 'We will not believe you until we see Allah', and we do not concede that the condition is possible; rather it is the settling of the mountain while it is moving, which is impossible?! Its answer: all of that is contrary to the apparent [meaning], so there is no reason to interpret it thus. For if his people were believers, his statement 'It is impossible' would suffice them; otherwise, they would not believe him in Allah's ruling of impossibility, so the question is frivolous in any case. And the settling while moving is possible in that stillness may occur instead of motion; it is only the combination of motion and stillness that is impossible.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage presents a scriptural proof (dalil sam'iyy) for the possibility (jawaz) of seeing Allah (ru'ya) based on the request of Moses in the Qur'an. The argument follows a logical sequence: (1) If ru'ya were impossible, Moses, being a prophet, would not have asked for it—since prophets are free from ignorance, foolishness, or frivolity in asking for the impossible. (2) Allah conditioned the response on a possible event (the mountain settling), and a condition attached to a possible thing must itself be possible; otherwise, God's word would be false. The objection from the Mu'tazila claims Moses' question was to teach his people that ru'ya is impossible, and that the condition (mountain settling while moving) is impossible. The answer refutes both: the interpretation is forced and against the apparent meaning; if the people were believers, Moses' assertion of impossibility would suffice, so the question would be pointless; and settling while moving is possible because stillness can replace motion—only the simultaneous combination of motion and stillness is impossible. Thus the original proof stands.

Key Terms

الدليل السمعي
استقرار الجبل
ممكن
محال
أنبياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume that prophets might ask for the impossible in order to teach a lesson to their people, even if the thing is impossible.
Correction: The passage argues that such a request would imply ignorance or frivolity, which is impossible for prophets. The apparent meaning of the request is that it is for seeking the actual vision, not for teaching.

Checkpoint
What is the main scriptural proof presented for the possibility of seeing Allah?
A) The consensus of the companions
B) Moses asking to see Allah in the Qur'an
C) The hadith about seeing the moon
D) The verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار'

Key Takeaway
Moses' request for vision of Allah, combined with the conditional upon the mountain's settling, provides a strong scriptural argument that ru'ya is possible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Moses (AS) desperately sought to see Allah, and his request became a proof for us that this vision is possible. How deep is your own longing to see Allah on the Day of Judgment? If it is weak, what worldly attachment or heedlessness is stealing that desire? Make a concrete plan today to revive that longing in your heart.
?
The objection against the proof claimed Moses was only teaching his people, not actually seeking vision. Are there areas in your life where you justify half-hearted worship or du'a by saying 'it's just for teaching' or 'it's just a ritual'? Examine your sincerity: is your prayer a real request from your Lord, or a hollow exercise?
?
Allah conditioned the vision on a possible event—the mountain's settling. Even when moving, stillness can replace motion. If you are in a state of spiritual 'motion' (distraction, sin), is it possible for stillness (tranquility, obedience) to take its place? What is the one change you will make this week to replace a destructive habit with stillness before Allah?

The Transmitted Proofs for Seeing Allah
Cites Qur'an, hadith, and early consensus for ru'ya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Qur'anic and hadith evidence for the believers' vision of Allah and the early consensus on this matter.

Core Idea
Seeing Allah is affirmed by Quran, hadith, and early consensus.

This lesson examines the transmitted proofs (dalil al-naql) for the reality of ru'ya. The author presents the key evidence from the Qur'an and Sunnah, and emphasizes that the early community agreed upon this without metaphorical interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the emphasis on consensus before innovations.
2
Identify the two categories of evidence
The passage cites a Qur'anic verse and a hadith. Find each and note how they are introduced.
The verse is from Surah al-Qiyamah, the hadith is about seeing the moon.
3
Reflect on the role of consensus
The author states the umma agreed on the literal meaning before innovations arose. Ask yourself why this consensus matters.
Consensus is a third pillar of evidence here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد أتى فيه) أي: في وقوع الرؤية للمؤمنينَ (دليلُ النَّقْلِ) مِنَ الكِتابِ والسُّنَةِ، وأجمعت الأمةُ على ذلك قبل ظهورِ البِدَعِ، بإبقاء النصوص الواردة على ظاهرها مِنْ تأويل، وكل ما هو كذلك فالجزْمُ به واجب. أمّا الكِتابُ فقوله تعالى: ﴿وُجُوهٌ يَوْمَئِذٍ نَاضِرَةٌ * إِلَى رَبِّهَا نَاظِرَةٌ﴾. وأمّا السُنَّةُ فَغيرُ ما حديث، مِنها قوله : (إِنَّكم ستَرُونَ رَبَّكُم كما تَرَونَ القَمَرَ لَيلةَ البدرِ) وهو حديث مشهورٌ. وخالف في ذلك المعتزلة، فأحالوها متمسكينَ بشُبَه (٦)، أقواها شبهة المقابلة، وأجيب عن ذلك بأن معنى لا تدركه لا تحيط به، على أنه قال لا تدركه ولم يقل لا تراه، فالأبصار لا تحيط به كما أن العقول لا تحيط به.
And there has come for it—i.e., for the occurrence of vision for the believers—the transmitted proof (dalil al-naql) from the Book and the Sunna, and the community (umma) has agreed upon that before the appearance of innovations, by keeping the texts as they appear without interpretation, and everything that is so, affirmation of it is obligatory. As for the Book, it is His exalted saying: 'Faces on that day are radiant, looking at their Lord.' And as for the Sunna, it is many hadiths, among them his saying: 'You will see your Lord as you see the moon on the night of the full moon,' and it is a well-known hadith. And the Mu'tazila opposed that, declaring it impossible, clinging to doubts, the strongest of which is the doubt of confrontation, and it was answered that the meaning of 'does not perceive Him' is 'does not encompass Him', for He said 'does not perceive' and did not say 'does not see', so eyesights do not encompass Him just as minds do not encompass Him.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage presents the transmitted (naqli) evidence for the reality of ru'ya for the believers. The author states that the consensus of the early community (before heretical innovations) was to take the relevant texts in their apparent meaning (zahir) without metaphorical interpretation (ta'wil), and that such texts must be affirmed with certainty. Two key proofs are cited: (1) Qur'an 75:22-23, 'وجوه يومئذ ناضرة * إلى ربها ناظرة' (Faces that day are radiant, looking at their Lord). (2) The well-known hadith that believers will see their Lord as clearly as the full moon. The Mu'tazila rejected ru'ya and relied on several doubts; the strongest is the 'shubhat al-muqabala' (the doubt of confrontation) from the verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار' (Sight does not perceive Him) (6:103). They argued that if Allah could be seen, He would be encompassed by sight, which would imply deficiency. The response distinguishes between 'idrak' (encompassment) and 'ru'ya' (seeing): the verse negates encompassment, not vision itself, just as the mind cannot fully comprehend Allah but can know Him. Thus the proof from the Qur'an and hadith is preserved, and the Mu'tazila objection is refuted.

Key Terms
دليل النقل
الرؤية
إجماع الأمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verses about seeing Allah are metaphorical and do not indicate literal vision.
Correction: The early consensus held the texts on their apparent meaning, affirming literal vision, as stated here: 'بإبقاء النصوص الواردة على ظاهرها من تأويل'.

Checkpoint
What does the author say about the community's stance before innovations?
A) They disagreed on the interpretation.
B) They agreed on the literal meaning without interpretation.
C) They only accepted the Qur'anic verse.
D) They rejected the hadith.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an and Sunnah clearly affirm that believers will see Allah, and the early community accepted this literally.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly long to see Allah as the believers will on that day, or are your desires consumed by worldly pleasures? What can you change today to redirect your heart toward that ultimate vision?
?
When you encounter a divine attribute that challenges your limited understanding, are you willing to submit to the apparent meaning of revelation as the Salaf did, or do you feel the urge to reinterpret? What would it cost you to simply trust Allah's words?
?
If the hadith says you will see Allah 'as you see the moon,' what does that tell you about the certainty and clarity you should have about this promise? How would your life look different if you truly believed this with full conviction?

The Mu'tazila Doubt and Its Refutation
Presents the Mu'tazila shubha and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila objection based on the verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار' and the refutation distinguishing encompassment from vision.

Core Idea
Sight does not encompass Allah, so negation of encompassment is not negation of vision.

The Mu'tazila rejected the vision of Allah by appealing to the verse 'Sight does not perceive Him.' This lesson presents their strongest doubt and shows how the response preserves the clear proofs for ru'ya by distinguishing between 'idrak' (encompassment) and 'ru'ya' (seeing).

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazila objection
Read the Arabic passage focusing on how the Mu'tazila use the verse to argue against ru'ya.
The doubt is called 'shubhat al-muqabala'.
2
Understand the response
The author responds by clarifying the meaning of 'idrak'. Notice the distinction between perception and encompassment.
The response also draws an analogy with the mind.
3
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how this refutation preserves the evidence from the previous lesson without contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And there has come for it—i.e., for the occurrence of vision for the believers—the transmitted proof (dalil al-naql) from the Book and the Sunna, and the community (umma) has agreed upon that before the appearance of innovations, by keeping the texts as they appear without interpretation, and everything that is so, affirmation of it is obligatory. As for the Book, it is His exalted saying: 'Faces on that day are radiant, looking at their Lord.' And as for the Sunna, it is many hadiths, among them his saying: 'You will see your Lord as you see the moon on the night of the full moon,' and it is a well-known hadith. And the Mu'tazila opposed that, declaring it impossible, clinging to doubts, the strongest of which is the doubt of confrontation, and it was answered that the meaning of 'does not perceive Him' is 'does not encompass Him', for He said 'does not perceive' and did not say 'does not see', so eyesights do not encompass Him just as minds do not encompass Him.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage presents the transmitted (naqli) evidence for the reality of ru'ya for the believers. The author states that the consensus of the early community (before heretical innovations) was to take the relevant texts in their apparent meaning (zahir) without metaphorical interpretation (ta'wil), and that such texts must be affirmed with certainty. Two key proofs are cited: (1) Qur'an 75:22-23, 'وجوه يومئذ ناضرة * إلى ربها ناظرة' (Faces that day are radiant, looking at their Lord). (2) The well-known hadith that believers will see their Lord as clearly as the full moon. Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the strongest doubt of the Mu'tazila according to this passage?
A) The hadith about the moon
B) The verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار'
C) The consensus of the companions
D) The impossibility of seeing without direction

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila doubt is refuted by recognizing that 'idrak' means encompassment, not sight, so the verse does not contradict ru'ya.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'لا تدركه الأبصار', do you feel a sense of distance from Allah, as if He is too far to be seen or known? How does this lesson's distinction between 'idrak' (encompassment) and 'ru'ya' (vision) change that feeling, and what does it demand from you in your prayer and longing for Him?
?
The Mu'tazila used their intellect to deny what the revelation clearly affirms. Where in your own life do you find yourself using your limited understanding to reject or reinterpret Allah's commands rather than submitting? What is one specific area where you need to surrender to Allah this week?
?
If Allah is not fully encompassed by sight, yet He will be seen by the believers, what does that mean for your hope of the afterlife? How does that hope shape your daily struggle to purify your heart and actions for that meeting?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
8 min
Attributes Derived from Divine Independence
Dardeer derives attributes from God's independence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how God's absolute self-sufficiency necessitates His essential attributes: existence, pre-eternity, perpetuity, dissimilarity to creation, self-subsistence, and transcendence above deficiencies, including hearing, sight, and speech.

Core Idea
God's independence directly entails His core attributes without dependence on anything.

This lesson explores the chain of reasoning that begins with God's oneness and self-sufficiency. Imam Dardeer shows how from God's independence we derive the foundational attributes that distinguish Him from all creation. The passage is a logical unfolding of necessary truths.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the first part of the passage (up to 'كيف وهو الغني بالإطلاق عن كل ما سواه') to grasp the logical flow from independence to attributes.
Notice the if-then structure: independence necessitates existence, pre-eternity, etc.
2
Identify the attributes from independence
List the attributes that follow from God's independence: existence, pre-eternity, perpetuity, dissimilarity to originated things, self-subsistence, transcendence, hearing, sight, speech, and negation of purposes and inherent power in creatures.
These are all necessary for a self-sufficient being.
3
Understand the reasoning
For each attribute, ask: why must God have it if He is independent? For example, if He were like created things, He would depend on others.
This shows the method of kalam: deriving attributes from a foundational concept.
4
Reflect on the negation of deficiencies
Notice that transcendence leads to positive attributes like hearing and sight, because lacking them would be a deficiency implying dependence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الثالث: السمعيات
وحده مفهوما، وهذا يستلزم استغناءه تعالى عن كل ما سواه، وافتقار كل ما سواه إليه تعالى.
أما استغناؤه عن كل ما سواه فيوجب له تعالى الوجود والقدم والبقاء ومخالفته تعالى للحوادث وقيامه بنفسه، إذ لو ماثل شيئًا منها للزمه ما لزمها من الافتقار وهو محال، ولو قام بغيره لكان مفتقرًا إلى ذلك الغير.
ويوجب له أيضًا التنزه عن النقائص، وهو يستلزم وجوب السمع والبصر والكلام، والتنزه عن الأغراض في الأفعال والأحكام، وإلا لكان مفتقرًا إلى ما يتكمل به من ذلك العرض (۳)، وعدم وجوب فعل شيء من الممكنات أو تركه (۳)، وعدم كون شيء من الممكنات يؤثر بقوة أودعها الله فيه، وإلا لم يكن مستغنيًا عن كل ما سواه، كيف وهو الغني بالإطلاق عن كل ما سواه.
وأما افتقار كل ما سواه إليه تعالى، فهو يوجب له تعالى القدرة والإرادة والعلم والحياة والوحدانية؛ لما تقدم من أن التعدد يوجب العجز. ويؤخذ منه حدوث العالم بأسره، ونفي تأثير شيء منه بالطبع أو بالعلة، وإذا وجب شيء استحال ضده. هذا حاصل ما بينه الإمام السنوسي رضي الله عنه.
ولك أن تقول: الله علم على الذات الواجب الوجود، الخالق للعالم، وقد دلت هذه الجملة على حضر الألوهية فيه تعالى، وظاهر أن كونه واجب الوجود وخالقا للعالم يتضمن جميع ما ذكر.
The third section: the sam'iyyat (audible matters). It alone as understood, and this necessitates His, may He be exalted, being independent of everything other than Him, and the dependence of everything other than Him upon Him, may He be exalted. As for His independence from everything other than Him, it necessitates for Him, may He be exalted, existence, pre-eternity, perpetuity, His being different from originated things, and His self-subsistence; for if He resembled any of them, what befell them of dependence would befall Him, and that is impossible, and if He subsisted through another, He would be dependent on that other. And it also necessitates for Him transcendence above deficiencies, and that necessitates the necessity of hearing, sight, and speech, and transcendence above purposes in actions and rulings; otherwise He would be dependent on what perfects Him through that accidental attribute, and the non-necessity of doing any contingent thing or leaving it, and the non-existence of any contingent thing having effect by a power that Allah placed in it; otherwise He would not be independent of everything other than Him; how could that be when He is absolutely independent of everything other than Him? And as for the dependence of everything other than Him upon Him, may He be exalted, that necessitates for Him, may He be exalted, power, will, knowledge, life, and oneness; because of what preceded that multiplicity necessitates incapacity. And from it is taken the origination of the entire world, and the negation of any effect from it by nature or by cause, and when something is necessary, its opposite becomes impossible. This is the gist of what Imam al-Sanusi, may Allah be pleased with him, explained. And you may say: Allah is a proper name for the essence that is necessary of existence, the creator of the world, and this sentence indicates the presence of divinity in Him, may He be exalted, and it is apparent that His being necessary of existence and creator of the world includes all that was mentioned.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal proof that derives the necessary divine attributes from the concept of God's absolute self-sufficiency and the total dependence of everything else. It begins by stating that the oneness of God implies His independence from all others and the dependence of all others on Him. The author then divides the reasoning: First, from God's independence, he derives the attributes of existence, pre-eternity, perpetuity, dissimilarity to originated things, self-subsistence, and transcendence above deficiencies. From transcendence he further derives the necessity of hearing, sight, speech, and transcendence above purposes, as well as the non-necessity of actions and the negation of inherent power in creatures. Second, from the dependence of all else on God, he derives power, will, knowledge, life, and oneness, because multiplicity implies incapacity. He also notes that this implies the origination of the world and the negation of natural or causal efficacy. The passage concludes with a summary from Imam al-Sanusi and an alternative concise formulation using the name 'Allah' as the necessary existent and creator.

Key Terms
الاستغناء
الوجود
القدم
البقاء
المخالفة للحوادث
القيام بالنفس
التنزه عن النقائص
السمع
البصر
الكلام
الأغراض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that deriving attributes from self-sufficiency implies a chain of entailments that compromises God's simplicity.
Correction: The attributes are necessary consequences of a single reality, not additions to His essence; they are affirmed without multiplicity in reality.

Checkpoint
Which attribute is NOT directly derived from God's independence in this passage?
A) Existence
B) Pre-eternity
C) Power
D) Self-subsistence

Key Takeaway
God's self-sufficiency logically entails all His essential attributes without any dependence on creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt that your worth or stability depends on something other than God—like people's approval, material possessions, or your own abilities? How does the truth of God's absolute independence challenge you to re-center your reliance solely on Him?
?
If God derives none of His attributes from anything outside Himself, why do you still look to creation to find your own identity and security? What would it look like for you to seek your sufficiency in God alone starting today?
?
The passage states that having purposes in actions implies dependence. In what areas of your life are you still acting with hidden agendas or seeking personal gain, even in worship? Are you willing to purify your intentions so that your actions reflect only God's independence and transcendence?

Divine Attributes

Attributes Derived from Creation's Dependence
Dardeer derives attributes from creation's dependence on God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the dependence of all creation on God necessitates His attributes of power, will, knowledge, life, oneness, and the implications for the world's origination and rejection of natural causality.

Core Idea
Creation's utter dependence proves God's absolute power, will, knowledge, life, and oneness.

This lesson looks at the second half of the passage, where Imam Dardeer explains what follows from the fact that everything other than God depends on Him. This dependence not only proves God's attributes but also shows the world must have been created and cannot act independently.

Guided Path
1
Read the second part of the passage
Read from 'وأما افتقار كل ما سواه إليه تعالى' to 'وإذا وجب شيء استحال ضده' to see the attributes derived from creation's dependence.
Notice the contrast: independence gave 'static' attributes; dependence gives 'active' attributes like power and will.
2
Identify the five attributes
List power, will, knowledge, life, and oneness. Ask why each is necessary for the One upon whom all depend.
For example, if God were not powerful, He could not provide what creatures need.
3
Understand the implications
Note that this also proves the world's origination (hadath) and negates any natural or causal efficacy in creation.
The phrase 'وإذا وجب شيء استحال ضده' links necessity to impossibility of opposite.
4
Connect to previous lesson
Reflect on how the two halves together give a complete picture of God's attributes.

Source Text

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This lesson proves that God must have knowledge, will, and power because of your dependence. If you truly believed that God's will is the sole cause of every event, would you fear anything else? What is the one fear you still hold that reveals you doubt this?
?
If the world's origination is taken from its dependence, then your own existence is a sign that you were brought from nothing. Have you internalized that you have no inherent right to exist—that your entire being is a gift sustained moment by moment? What would change in your life if you felt this reality every second?

The Summary in the Divine Name
Dardeer summarizes the creed via the name 'Allah'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the name 'Allah' encapsulates all the divine attributes derived from self-sufficiency and creation's dependence.

Core Idea
The name 'Allah' means the Necessary Existent and Creator, implicitly containing all attributes.

In this final lesson, Imam Dardeer provides a concise summary of the entire creed. He connects the theological derivations back to the name 'Allah' itself, showing that the simple statement 'Allah is the necessary existent and creator' includes all the attributes discussed. This serves as a beautiful closure to the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the concluding paragraph
Read from 'هذا حاصل ما بينه الإمام السنوسي' to the end to see how the creed is summarized.
Notice the two names: 'واجب الوجود' and 'خالق العالم' are key.
2
Understand the summary function
The author says that the name 'Allah' indicates the essence that is Necessary Existence and Creator, which includes all that was mentioned.
This shows the economy of Islamic theology: a single name implies much.
3
Reflect on the connection to previous lessons
Think about how the attributes from independence and dependence are both contained in 'Necessary Existence' and 'Creator'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Two Kinds of Tajalli: Attributes and Actions
Explains two examples of tajalli: with attribute of hearing and with actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two distinct types of divine manifestations (tajalli) described after fana: the unveiling of God's attributes (like hearing) and the unveiling of His actions, along with the spiritual insights they bring.

Core Idea
Tajalli reveals either God's attributes or His actions, each granting unique perceptions.

After the state of fana, the wayfarer may experience divine unveilings (tajalli). The author of this text describes two kinds: one where the divine attribute of hearing is manifested, enabling one to hear the speech of inanimate objects, and another where God's actions are manifested, showing His power as the sole mover and stiller. This lesson unpacks these two manifestations and their spiritual implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on tajalli
Read the Arabic passage once, focusing on the two examples given. Then read the translation.
2
Identify the first type (attributes)
Notice the example of the attribute of hearing. What does the wayfarer experience? Reflect on the meaning of hearing inanimate objects.
3
Identify the second type (actions)
Now focus on the manifestation with actions. What is disclosed? Note the warning that this is a slippery place.
The author cautions that this manifestation can lead to negating human action entirely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ينجلي لقلبه من صفاته تعالى، فمثلا إذا تجلى الحق عليه بصفة السمع صار يسمع نطق الجمادات وغيره، وإذا تجلى الحق على السالك بأفعاله انكشف له جريان قدرة الله تعالى في الأشياء، فيرى أنه تعالى هو المحرك وهو المسكن شهودا حاليا لا يعرفه إلا أهله، وهذا التجلي مزلة الأقدام فيخشى على السالك منه لأنه ينفي الفعل عن العبد بالكلية، ولكن يُثَبِّتُ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا بِالْقَوْلِ الثَّابِت في الحَيَاةِ الدُّنْيَا وَفِي الآخِرَةِ [إبراهيم: ٢٧] واعلم أن تجلي الأفعال سابق على تجلي الصفات والأسماء، فإذا ثبت السالك ترقى إلى تجلي الأسماء والصفات، وإن لم يثبت تزندق ورجع من الطريق.
There unveils for his heart from the attributes of the Most High. For example, when the Truth manifests to him with the attribute of hearing, he begins to hear the speech of inanimate objects and other things. And when the Truth manifests to the wayfarer with His actions, there is disclosed to him the flow of the power of God Most High in things, and he sees that He Most High is the mover and the stiller in a present witnessing that only its people know. And this manifestation is a slippery place for feet, so it is feared for the wayfarer from it because it negates the action from the servant entirely. But God establishes those who believe with the firm word in the life of the world and the Hereafter [Ibrahim 14:27]. And know that the manifestation of actions precedes the manifestation of attributes and names. So if the wayfarer becomes steadfast, he ascends to the manifestation of names and attributes; and if he does not become steadfast, he becomes a heretic and returns from the path.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage explains the spiritual unveilings (tajalli) that occur after fana. It describes two types: manifestation with the attribute of hearing, allowing one to hear the speech of inanimate objects, and manifestation with actions, revealing God's power in all things. The author warns that this latter tajalli is dangerous because it can lead to negating the servant's actions entirely (determinism). He cites the Quranic verse affirming steadfastness. He then states that the tajalli of actions precedes that of attributes and names. If the wayfarer remains steadfast, he ascends; if not, he falls into heresy and abandons the path.

Key Terms
تجلي
صفات
أفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that witnessing God's actions means humans have no free will at all.
Correction: The author warns this is a slippery slope but does not deny human action entirely; rather, one must remain steadfast and recognize that God's power encompasses all, while human actions are not negated in the proper perspective.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the wayfarer experience when the Truth manifests with the attribute of hearing?
A) He sees the divine throne
B) He hears the speech of inanimate objects
C) He becomes omniscient
D) He loses all senses

Key Takeaway
The wayfarer after fana may experience tajalli of divine attributes (like hearing) or tajalli of divine actions, each revealing unique aspects of God's reality, but the second requires caution.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe events unfolding in your life, do you see them as purely from God or do you acknowledge your own choices? How does this lesson challenge you to keep both in balance?
?
Imagine you had a direct spiritual experience of God's control over everything. Would you be tempted to stop striving and blame outcomes on fate? What safeguard does this passage offer against that?
?
If you have ever felt that your actions were meaningless because 'God does it all,' how can you correct that belief using the Quranic verse cited here? Be specific: what action will you take today to affirm both God's power and your responsibility?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
4 min
The Order of Unveilings: Actions Precede Attributes
States the order of tajalli and the two outcomes of steadfastness vs. heresy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct sequence of divine manifestations after fana: the unveiling of actions must precede that of attributes and names, and the consequences of steadfastness or deviation.

Core Idea
The tajalli of actions comes first; steadfastness leads to higher unveilings, while failure leads to heresy.

Having described the types of tajalli, the author now establishes a critical order: the manifestation of divine actions comes before the manifestation of attributes and names. This lesson explains this sequence and emphasizes the importance of spiritual steadfastness to avoid falling into heresy.

Guided Path
1
Read the final part of the passage
Read the Arabic and translation about the order of tajalli and the two outcomes.
2
Identify the order
Notice the explicit statement: 'the manifestation of actions precedes the manifestation of attributes and names.'
3
Understand the consequence of steadfastness
The passage says if the wayfarer becomes steadfast, he ascends to higher tajalli; if not, he becomes a heretic and leaves the path.
This underscores the danger of the tajalli of actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that all types of tajalli can occur simultaneously or in any order.
Correction: The author explicitly states that the tajalli of actions must come first, and the wayfarer must pass through it before the higher manifestations.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if the wayfarer is steadfast after experiencing the tajalli of actions?
A) He immediately attains union with God
B) He ascends to the tajalli of names and attributes
C) He returns to worldly life
D) He becomes a prophet

Key Takeaway
The manifestation of actions precedes that of attributes and names; steadfastness is essential to avoid heresy and progress to higher stations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness God's actions in your life—especially events that challenge your sense of control—do you remain steadfast in recognizing your own responsibility, or do you feel a pull toward denying your agency? What concrete step can you take today to strengthen your steadfastness?
?
This passage warns that failing to be steadfast after the first unveiling leads to heresy and leaving the path. Is there a spiritual insight you once received that you later abandoned because it unsettled you? What would it cost you to return to that insight with firmness?
?
The order here is deliberate: actions before attributes before names. Are you impatient for higher spiritual states while neglecting the foundational work of witnessing God's actions with proper faith? How will you adjust your priorities tomorrow?
